Inaugural Address

Publicizing Telecommunications 87

— Lü Bing

In today's world, the words "public" and "open" have become fashionable terms. Listing income and expenditure is financial transparency; appointing people based on their abilities is open recruitment. For all other measures, if we can conduct open research based on factual circumstances, credibility will be established, and results will be achieved with half the effort. This can be stated definitively. Telecommunications in our country has a history of over fifty years. From its establishment to its expansion, it has gradually evolved into the phenomenon we see today. Progress has been slow, which is undeniable. However, looking back, we often lament the obstacles that have hindered the advancement of the industry. Telecommunications itself is not to blame. Moreover, past administrations, in their approach to telecommunications reform, revealed only a glimpse, keeping it closely guarded. Even when telecommunications experts conducted research and discussions, they often failed to attract public attention. In fact, the common perception was that telecommunications was a profitable state-run enterprise, requiring no specialized skills to manage effectively, leading to officials engaging in malfeasance to satisfy their personal greed. With the industry lacking transparency and its inner workings concealed, the public viewed telecommunications as a mystery. This publication aims to dispel this mystery.

An industry cannot be divorced from society, and the use of telecommunications is deeply connected to the public. Now that the political situation is gradually becoming clearer and the authorities are striving for development, telecommunications is an important part of that development. In this phase of growth, it is felt that public discussion is valuable to meet society's needs. The staff of this publication is committed to the following goals: We will strive to uncover and report on telecommunications development news so that the public can understand the truth. We will strive to contribute opinions on telecommunications reform so that the authorities know what to adopt. In addition, we will fully publish general telecommunications knowledge, skills, recent developments in overseas telecommunications, and the latest statistics on China's telecommunications, to introduce them to the public. If members of the public have opinions on the use of telecommunications, their publication can assist those working in the telecommunications industry. In short, we aim to make "telecommunications" public, and through the power of society, promote the development of the telecommunications industry. The "Publicizing Telecommunications" initiative is intended for this purpose. Therefore, at the beginning of this publication, we have chosen these four characters as our motto.

Controlled Economy and Telecommunications 88

— Wang Yunzhen

Since the Mukden Incident, the tide of global economic panic has swept across the Pacific, impacting our country, which suffers from insufficient production, underdeveloped industry, and inadequate transportation, the most. Examining our national situation internally and considering the external environment, we realize that unity is essential to resist foreign aggression, and development is necessary to alleviate the people's suffering. First, Wang Jingwei issued a declaration to "seek unity through development," followed by Song Ziwen's plan to "save the country from its economic woes." Consequently, the Economic Commission was reorganized, hoping to strengthen national power through controlled economic methods and break through the internal and external pressures. This is indeed the only nation-saving policy permissible under China's current circumstances.

What is a controlled economy? Chinese scholars are divided on the issue. Mr. Wu Daquan said: "A controlled economy is when a country, under a certain economic doctrine, creates a comprehensive and systematic economic plan for a specific purpose, whether temporarily or permanently, within a certain economic organization, and implements it using the power of the state." Mr. Mu Qichu said: "The cornerstone of a controlled economy lies in the shift from instability to stability, from operation to management, from the unknown to the known. This is the mainstream of economic development and the continuous effort of all economic actors, as well as the path forward for a controlled economy." Mr. Zheng Dubu believes that a controlled economy is when the state, for the purpose of harmonizing national life and developing the national economy, rationally controls the entirety of national economic activity, eliminates contradictions and conflicts in economic behavior. Based on these three views, we can draw a conclusion: A controlled economy is when a country, under a certain economic environment, uses state power to formulate an economic plan for the purpose of stabilizing national life, alleviating economic panic, and harmonizing national production, in order to achieve economic equilibrium in society.

Does China need to implement economic controls? We need not look as far back as Guan Zhong's rule of Qi, Shang Yang's rule of Qin, or Wang Anshi's rule of Song, which are authoritative examples of controlled economies in history. Reading Sun Yat-sen's "The International Development of China," which aims to develop national production, reveals the fundamental principle of a controlled economy. Furthermore, according to Article 19 of the Domestic Policy Program of the First National Congress of the Kuomintang, "Enterprises with monopolistic characteristics that cannot be run by private individuals, such as railways and shipping, shall be managed by the state." The so-called enterprises with monopolistic characteristics refer to transportation and public utilities. Telecommunications is one of the transportation industries, which is significantly related to a nation’s political, military, economic, and cultural affairs. For this reason, our government nationalized the telecommunications industry 25 years ago (the 34th year of the Guangxu reign in the Qing Dynasty), taking it from private hands through sound legislation. However, in the past 25 years, the telecommunications industry has declined and various contradictions and conflicts have been discovered. This is not a fault of the telecommunications system itself, but a failure of control.

Regarding the legal aspects of telecommunications control, there is the Telecommunications Ordinance promulgated by the National Government on August 5, 1929; the Regulations on the Supervision of Private Public Utilities promulgated in December of the same year; and the Provisional Measures for Import Permits for Wireless Radio Materials approved on May 8, 1930. On January 31, 1930, the Executive Yuan issued a circular to all agencies in Beijing and elsewhere to ban privately established radio stations, and on July 7, 1933, approved the Ministry of Communications' principle of entrusting provincial governments to handle long-distance telephone services. Among the regulations promulgated by the Ministry of Communications are the Regulations on the Prohibition of Private Submarine Cables Landing, dated December 24, 1930, and the Provisional Regulations on the Prohibition of Private Broadcasting Radio Stations, dated November 24, 1933. A close reading of these regulations reveals the significance of controlled economic measures, strict legislation, and self-respect for sovereignty. However, what is the actual situation?

The landing of submarine cables concerns national sovereignty, and foreigners should not be allowed to set them up privately without the permission of the host country's government. Since 1865 (the fourth year of the Tongzhi reign in the Qing Dynasty), when a Briton named Laying installed a landline from Shanghai to Wusongkou, a gradual encroachment on sovereignty had begun. Later, in 1871 (the tenth year of the Tongzhi reign), the Great Northern Telegraph Company privately installed a submarine cable in Shanghai, connecting it to Xiamen, Hong Kong in the south, and Nagasaki and Vladivostok in the north. Under the condition of letting China use its cables, the Qing court permitted it, giving foreign companies legal acknowledgement to the landing of submarine cables. Then various water cable landing and connection contracts, water cable landing patent contracts, Shanghai-Yan-Gu water cable agency contracts, Gu-Jin-Ping cable borrowing contracts, loan contracts, and reporting fee contracts were signed. The conditions were harsh and extremely restrictive, preventing the development of external communications. Fortunately, various unequal treaties have expired. After two years of negotiations by the Ministry of Communications, a new treaty was signed this April, recovering many rights and interests. However, it would be imprudent to say that sovereignty has been completely restored. This is evidence that international wired telegraphy has failed to implement controlled economic policies.

During the time of the Beijing government, domestic wired telegraph bureaus were controlled by local military men, and the bureau chiefs were their cronies. The central government simply made appointments as usual. With the establishment of the National Government, there was a refreshing change. But due to various reasons, the military separatist situation could not be entirely broken. The chiefs of the telegraph bureaus in Guangdong, Guangxi, Sichuan, Yunnan, and Guizhou provinces were all appointed by local military men. The reporting fee revenues and various forms were often not submitted to the Ministry for review. Because political unification was not achieved, the telecommunications industry lost the opportunity for control.

Although domestic wireless telegraph and telephone services are managed by the Ministry of Communications, the Construction Departments of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Shandong, Henan, Hunan, Hubei, Guangdong, Guangxi and other provinces also operate provincial long-distance telephone services, using telephone telegraphs and competing with the Ministry for short-term profits. Or, under the pretext of military communications, they set up shortwave radio stations and secretly send and receive commercial reports, which is also common. As for foreigners in the concessions or foreign consulates setting up radio stations to transmit news, this is even more disruptive to our national sovereignty. Methods should be devised to ban these practices in order to achieve effective control.

The most advantageous aspect of economic control is the development of transportation. And the easiest way to develop transportation is to reorganize existing industries and plan new initiatives. China's telecommunications industry has a history of 50 years and more than 20,000 specialized personnel. If reorganized and expanded, it would be easier than various other transportation industries. Its function is to hold the communications hub for various transportation industries. We must formulate fundamental telecommunications laws and lay the administrative foundation. Allocate a portion of the cotton and wheat loan to serve as the economic foundation. Then unify the telecommunications organization and train capable personnel. Adhere to the principle of economic control, and use the method of technical cooperation to formulate a ten-year or five-year telecommunications implementation plan. Persevere and be determined to fully implement it. If, after all this, China's telecommunications industry still cannot achieve the effectiveness of economic control, I will not believe it.

Phantom Circuit and Crossover in Telephone Communication ▲ A Simple Explanation 89

— Guan

I recently read in the newspapers that "For the sake of developing Beijing-Shanghai long-distance telephone service, four new telephone lines have been erected, and phantom crossovers are being used. This project is already underway and the phantom circuit will be operational

in the new year." The concept of phantom crossover may not be clear to many readers, and the benefits of using phantom circuits for Beijing-Shanghai long-distance telephone service are probably what readers want to know. Therefore, I will provide a simple explanation within the scope of this publication:

What is a phantom? This must be explained first. If something can be called a phantom, it seems to be virtually nonexistent. If we use the term "phantom," the image or sound seems unreal, which may cause misunderstanding. But in telephone usage, "phantom" is a technical term. Using a phantom circuit (a circuit is the path connecting both sides of a telephone call), if you originally have two pairs of telephone lines, this method can increase the number of usable pairs to three. There is no need to increase the number of lines or the induction of electrical current

, and simultaneous calls can be increased by one. The so-called phantom does not have a dedicated line for your own call, but rather uses the adjacent telephone line pair to connect and form a circuit. Not only is the call genuine, but it is also clearer. It is simply called a "phantom."

To understand the connection of a phantom circuit, you can refer to the diagram below. The two-way call in the middle of the diagram is the "phantom circuit," which is clearly different from the telephone sets at the top and bottom, each occupying a pair of wires.

Whether they are telegraph or telephone wires, if they are strung on the same pole, they can easily cause mutual induction. This induction is what ordinary people call noise. For example, when listening on the telephone, hearing the sound of telegraph transmissions or the voices of people talking nearby is induction. To reduce or eliminate induction, telecommunications uses a type of line crossover. This method involves crossing the wires every few poles, which is called a regular crossover. Alternatively, the phantom circuit mentioned above can be used. Because there are more lines, the crossover method is also different. This article is simply a brief explanation, so I will not elaborate on how to perform the crossover.

Readers can refer to the diagram below. The original wires above, due to the passage of current, cause induced electricity on lines A and B. This induced electricity is different at the top and bottom. Because of the crossover, the positive and negative charges tend to cancel each other out. Therefore, the impact on the two-way call can also be reduced. The reason why the Ministry of Communications of our country handles long-distance telephone service and uses crossovers on the Beijing-Shanghai line is to ensure that the caller can have a clear transmission, as if they were face to face.

Improvement of Telegraph Services in the Past Year (Part 1) Liu Junxiang 90

Telegraph is a public utility, and in terms of business, we should strive to commercialize it to facilitate communication for all parties. However, those who handled telecommunications in our country in the past often regarded the telegraph bureau as a state agency, as a means to becoming officials, leading to passivity, languor, and a sluggish atmosphere. As a result, there has been no significant progress in the past forty or fifty years. And the corruption of the content is particularly criticized by society. Recently, the Ministry of Communications, in order to rectify the situation, has been actively seeking the development of telegraph services under the principle of commercialization. It has thoroughly reformed the various abuses that existed in the past. On the one hand, it is adopting the current good practices in Europe and the United States as much as possible. Within the past year, the results of the improvement have been remarkable. Here are some of the major ones, listed as follows:

(1) Free Translation of Incoming Telegrams According to regulations, the telegraph bureaus used to require senders or recipients to translate telegrams received or sent. If someone requested the telegraph bureau to translate for them, they had to pay a translation fee. However, in fact, few senders and recipients, except for government agencies or large merchants, have code books. If it is a sending telegram, it can be translated by the telegraph bureau. But if it is an incoming telegram, the recipient has to take the telegram to the telegraph bureau after receiving it and ask for translation, which inevitably delays the matter. Furthermore, the scope of telegraph use in our country is very narrow. The general public does not send telegrams unless it is urgent. How anxious must the recipient be when they receive an untranslated telegram? The Ministry of Communications originally had a method for translating incoming telegrams, but over time it was neglected, and many bureaus and stations often disobeyed in secret. Therefore, the previous order has been reiterated, and penalties for missed translations have been stipulated: All incoming telegrams in Chinese, except for telegrams related to political news, disaster relief, and public welfare, and telegrams where the recipient is a merchant in a busy location, will be translated by the telegraph bureau free of charge. If it is found that a translation is missed, the person in charge will be fined one cent per word. At the same time, advertisements will be placed in various newspapers and periodicals to inform the public and prevent the bureaus and stations from deliberately trying to be clever. Afterwards, when recipients receive telegrams, they will immediately know the contents in detail, saving the trouble of translation and eliminating extra expenses. The benefits are indeed significant.

(2) Improving the Attitude of Receiving and Sending Personnel The receiving and sending personnel of each bureau and station have the most contact with the outside world. However, these personnel often have arrogant attitudes, and they often do not ask for details when answering questions. Furthermore, when charging fees, the exchange rates of various subsidiary coins are often arbitrarily changed, which can easily create a bad impression of the bureaus and stations among senders and is a major obstacle to the development of the business. The Ministry of Communications has specially formulated a "Receiving and Sending Personnel On-Duty Guidelines," which specifies in detail the matters that receiving and sending personnel should pay attention to, abide by, and understand while on duty, and distributed it to each bureau and station, so that the responsible personnel can earnestly supervise their compliance. Now, the receiving and sending personnel in various places are generally more polite, and they will answer inquiries to the best of their ability. The original undesirable practices have been eliminated, and senders feel much more convenient.

(3) Establishing Business Inspectors The regulations and procedures for telegrams are quite complicated, and many senders and recipients do not fully understand them. If they are not explained, misunderstandings can easily occur. Furthermore, it is inevitable that there are defects in business and errors in procedures on the telegraph bureau side. However, if there is no opportunity to communicate, one side will feel disappointed, and the other will not have any hope of improvement. In view of this, the Ministry of Communications has specially established business inspectors in each major bureau and station to be responsible for inspecting telegraph business. Every day, they personally go to various sending merchants, government agencies, organizations, newspaper offices, news agencies, etc. to inquire about incoming and outgoing telegrams. Are there any delays or errors? Are the various regulations and procedures clear? Are there any dissatisfactions? And pay attention to whether the bureaus and stations translate private Chinese telegrams? Are there any requests for tips from the couriers? From now on, if senders and recipients do not understand the telegraph business, they will have a place to ask questions. If there are any dissatisfactions, they will be able to get proper answers. Invisibly, a good impression of the telegraph bureaus and stations is fostered. And on the bureau and station side, they can also know where the shortcomings are and use them as a reference for improvement, which is truly a win-win situation.

Progress of French Broadcasting Radio Business Chen Xianding 91

French advanced scholars have made many contributions to the broadcasting radio business in their laboratory work. However, because the French people do not pay much attention to this important invention, the French broadcasting radio business has gradually lagged behind other developed countries. Therefore, the French people are now paying close attention to this business in order to regain their previous advantageous position.

The initial creation of the French broadcasting radio business was the broadcast of the Eiffel Tower military radio station in November 1921. This broadcast initially consisted only of weather reports, but soon included the dissemination of public economic and administrative news. Since then, there have been many important improvements over the past twelve years.

The question of whether the broadcasting of wireless telephones should be of a free or proprietary nature has become a problem. The Finance Act of June 30, 1923, stipulated that "the patent and security measures for telegraph lines stipulated in the order of December 27, 1851, shall apply to the transmission and reception of all radio signals." The order of December 28, 1926, stipulated the rules for state-run and private radio stations. The Finance Act of March 19, 1928, stipulated that the government had the right to temporarily permit private broadcasting radio businesses, limited to those that existed at the end of 1927. However, if there were any changes to the nature or method of operation, a special permit would be required to avoid conflicting with the organizational law of the broadcasting radio business. But even under these chaotic circumstances, private radio stations have made many improvements in organizational aspects, and in terms of funding, they have not received any national subsidies other than relying on their sole source of income, advertising revenue. Officials of the Postal and Telecommunications Department first created a state-run radio communications network, which received a small subsidy from the state in addition to collecting advertising revenue.

Regarding the regulations, each minister has planned and formulated them. During Martin's tenure, a free broadcasting jurisdiction was stipulated (May 28, 1929). Finally, the method of operating the broadcasting business with national financial resources was stipulated.

It is now planned to use 65 million francs to purchase or establish important broadcasting stations in various places as state-run businesses. And the Higher School of Posts and Telecommunications will increase the antenna power to 120KW to facilitate listeners in the countryside around Paris. The stations in Nice, Toulouse, and Lyon are planned to be 60KW. Other stations will also be improved.

The colonial broadcasting city station of Bon Mesa (near Paris), as well as the colonial stations in Algiers, Rabat, and Saigon, have all been opened. In addition, there are several other colonies that will also establish stations in the same way.

The French state-run radio communications network, within the country, includes the Higher School of Posts and Telecommunications, the Eiffel Tower, Lyon, Strasbourg, Grenoble, Marseille, Bordeaux, Montpelier, Rennes, Lille, Toulouse, and Limoges.

As for private stations, two have been approved to increase their power. In addition, Radio Paris of the French Radio Telephone Company has increased its antenna power from 17KW to 60KW, which can be called one of the largest stations in Europe. Poste-Parisien of the Power General Company was originally created by a major newspaper in Paris, and its antenna power has also been set at 60KW, which can compete with the best stations in Europe. Other similar methods have also been decided. There are currently ten private stations allowed to broadcast in France.

The order of December 28, 1926, stipulated that the technical aspects of the state-run broadcasting radio communications network are to be handled by the organs that manage finance and economy. But the arrangement and realization of the programs are entrusted to the following private businesses: such as the Radio Listeners Association (specifically for the Higher School of Posts and Telecommunications) and the General Radio Telephone Association (specifically for the Eiffel Tower). It is heard that the improvement of the organization is already mature, and the progress will inevitably be rapid. In the future, the French broadcasting radio business will have even greater progress.

The Significance of Recapturing the Telegraph Sending and Receiving Rights of Submarine Cable Companies He Shui 92

Based on equal telegraph contracts signed with the Qing government, the people of the three countries of Great Britain, Denmark, and the United States previously installed submarine cables in China's territorial waters, and separately established the Great Eastern, Great Northern, and Pacific three submarine cable companies in Shanghai, directly sending and receiving telegrams to and from Shanghai and various places in the world. Due to the length of their existence and their efforts to promote telegraph business, the names of these three companies are deeply imprinted in the minds of Shanghai residents, and when they have telegrams to send abroad, they must go to these companies to send them.

Because the previously signed unequal telecommunications contracts have expired, after strict negotiations between the Ministry of Communications and these companies, under the current national strength and financial environment, the first step is to recapture the rights of the companies to directly send and receive telegrams to the public. The reception of the three companies' sending and receiving offices will be implemented on May 1 of this year. They will be reorganized into "Sending and Receiving Offices for Great Eastern, Great Northern, and Pacific Submarine Cable Telegraphs of the International Telecommunications Bureau of the Ministry of Communications." The affairs within the offices, such as the sending and receiving of telegrams, the deployment of staff, and the management of couriers, will all be managed by the directors and deputy directors dispatched by the Ministry of Communications, acting under the orders of the Ministry of Communications and the International Telecommunications Bureau.

The recapture of the right to directly send and receive telegrams by submarine cable companies is of great significance, because from now on, all Chinese and foreign telegrams that are transmitted via the Great Eastern, Great Northern, and Pacific submarine cables will pass through our hands, and there will be no omission of a single telegram. Its greatest significance can be listed in the following points:

(A) Maintaining China's telecommunications sovereignty.

China's telecommunications is a state-run business and is managed by the Ministry of Communications. No other organization can overstep its authority. Foreign merchants, with the permission of the Chinese government and in compliance with the regulations promulgated by the Chinese government, are allowed to operate international telegraph communication businesses in China, which is not uncommon in Europe, the United States, and Japan. However, in order to maintain the integrity of China's telecommunications sovereignty, it is difficult to allow companies to directly send and receive telegrams to the outside world for a long time. (To be continued)

Information on Telegraph Inquiries 清hua 93

In this article, the terms "telegraph office" or "telegraph bureau," etc., can represent "radio station" or "radio station." For simplicity, we only use "telegraph office," new readers please note.

Telegrams are a powerful communication tool. Senders must be familiar with all telegraph business procedures in order to fully utilize them and achieve the greatest effectiveness. Because the Chinese people rarely send telegrams, they do not pay much attention to the various business procedures. The telegraph offices also rarely publicize, leaving the public without the opportunity to understand. Recently, the Ministry of Communications published a new edition of the Clear and Cipher Code, which includes detailed business procedures, providing great convenience to the public who have this book. However, the various business procedures published in this new edition of the code are mostly summaries of various telegraph regulations, and information regarding the procedures for inquiring about telegrams, etc., are still lacking. To facilitate the public and maximize the effectiveness of telegrams, we have specially compiled a "Guide to Telegraph Inquiries," which lists in detail the common knowledge that recipients or senders should have when inquiring about telegrams for reference. It is hoped that the telegraph offices will print this as a booklet and distribute it to telegram senders, so they can be familiar with how to use telegrams effectively, which will be beneficial to business development. (1) Guide to Telegraph Inquiries for Recipients

(1) Ambiguity in the Telegram Text: When a recipient receives a telegram, if there is ambiguity in a sentence or word in the text because it is not coherent with the overall meaning, or if they believe a word is incorrect, they can bring the telegram to the telegraph office for inquiry. If the office verifies that there is no error, a paid public telegram can be sent to the sending office to inquire. This paid public telegram is charged according to the number of characters being inquired about. For example, inquiring about one character requires prepayment of the fee for one character. If the inquiry reveals that the character was indeed transmitted incorrectly by the sending office or an intermediate office, the prepaid fee for one character can be refunded in full. However, if the character is correct, or if it was mistaken for another character due to the sender's unclear handwriting, the fee for this character will not be refunded.

(Note) If a recipient suspects ambiguity in the telegram text and inquires directly with the sender without using a paid public telegram, even if the character in question was indeed an error by the telegraph office, the fee for their own telegram and the original telegram fee will not be refunded.

(2) Missing Text in the Telegram: When a recipient receives a telegram and believes that there are missing words or sentences in the text, they can bring the telegram to the telegraph office for inquiry. If the office did not miss any transcription, it must have been a deletion by the sending office or an intermediate office. A paid public telegram can be sent to the sending office to inquire. There are two ways to inquire: (1) If it is believed that one or more characters are missing after a certain character, the request can be made to retransmit one or more characters after that character. (2) If many words or sentences are missing from the entire telegram, or if the meaning of the entire telegram is unclear, a request can be made to retransmit the entire telegram. This paid public telegram is charged according to the number of characters requested for retransmission. For example, requesting the retransmission of two characters requires prepayment of the fee for two characters. Requesting the retransmission of the entire telegram requires prepayment of the fee for all characters. If the inquiry reveals that the telegraph office did indeed miss one or more characters, the prepaid fee can be refunded in full. However, if among the retransmitted characters, only one character was missed by the telegraph office, and the remaining characters are the same as the original telegram, only the fee for one character will be refunded. (To be continued)

Breaking Away from Politics and Devoting to Construction 102

Cotton and Wheat Loans are Controlled by the Economic Council 105

In the future, all project expenses will be controlled by the American cotton and wheat loans. The rumors that the government has suffered losses in American cotton are completely untrue. The government will sell the American cotton after it is shipped and then continue to ship American cotton after it is sold out. American wheat will be shipped from the United States according to domestic needs. The first batch of American wheat is expected to be shipped from the United States to Shanghai around the end of the year or early next year. In short, the government has a detailed plan for selling American wheat and will never suffer any losses.

Resolution of the Refusal to Dye Wave The Two Parties Signed Three Reconciliation Measures The Trade Union Will Hold a Meeting Today to Discuss Resumption of Work 112

The Dagong News Agency reports that the workers in the silk and cloth dyeing industry in this city were indignant because the capital side did not fulfill the contract for the price list of wine money signed by the Agricultural, Industrial, and Commercial Bureau before the 16th year of the Republic of China, which caused a dispute over the refusal to dye goods in 72 dyeing workshops throughout the city. Yesterday, the Social Bureau convened a mediation and signed three reconciliation measures, announcing the resolution. The labor side is scheduled to hold a meeting today to discuss the resumption of work. The details are recorded as follows:

Mediation and Resolution The Social Bureau, considering that the dispute in the dyeing industry has been delayed and unresolved, and both parties have suffered infinite losses, specially convened a mediation again yesterday in conjunction with the Municipal Party Department. Wei Yi and Hu Taiqing from the labor side, Pan Zhongming and Fan Ruihua from the capital side, and Lu Yinchu from the Municipal Party Department attended. Zhu Jintao presided over the meeting and Wang Zhiqin took the minutes. First, the two parties stated their opinions. After a long period of negotiation, the opinions of the two parties gradually approached, and they expressed mutual supervision and implementation, and decided on three reconciliation measures as follows: (1) The wine money for silk and cloth dyeing workshops should be strictly implemented by the capital side in accordance with the price list of wine money signed by the Agricultural, Industrial, and Commercial Bureau before the 16th year of the Republic of China. (2) The above wine money will be collected by the trade union from the workshops between the 5th and 9th of each month and paid to the employees of each workshop in full immediately. (3) All silk and cloth city employees in the city should resume normal work before the 20th of this month. Both parties expressed their agreement and signed the minutes, announcing that the mediation was successful.

Labor Side Holds a Meeting The Municipal Dyeing Industry Trade Union believes that the silk dispute has been resolved by the Social Bureau, and all goods should resume work and be dyed as usual. Therefore, it has scheduled a meeting today to announce the mediation process and determine the date of resumption of work, and will then notify all silk workers to resume normal work.

Yesterday was the Republic Day of Brazil The Consulate Hosted Overseas Chinese 113

The Continental News reports that today (the 15th) is the 44th anniversary of Brazil's declaration of the Republic. Brazilians in Shanghai and around the world are celebrating. According to the Brazilian government's order last year, September 7 is National Day, because on that day in 1882, the Prince Regent declared Brazil's independence and called himself Emperor Pedro. On November 15, 1889, Brazil declared the Republic, but considering the value and relationship of independence, it was considered more important than declaring the Republic, so September 7 was used to replace November 15 as National Day. However, there are still celebrations as usual today, so the Brazilian Consul General in Shanghai and Brazilian Consular Judge in China, Amitada, held a meeting at the new consulate at 359 Gaun Road in the French Concession to host the residents of Shanghai.

The Banking Association Invited Dai Ailu to Speak on the National Crisis Views of Japan and China Japan is Tensely Working Hard to Prepare China is a Country Invaded But is As Calm as Usual 118

The Xinsheng News Agency reports that the Banking Association invited Dai Ailu, manager of the Osaka branch of the Bank of China, to give a lecture at the auditorium of the YMCA on Sichuan Road at 7:00 the day before yesterday. More than 300 members from various banks attended. Wang Zhixin, manager of Xinhua Bank, presided over the meeting and introduced Dai to the stage to report on his feelings after spending half a year in Japan and recently observing the situation in the three northeastern provinces and North China. His words were extremely insightful. The following is a record of his main ideas:

Atmosphere of National Crisis Mr. Dai first said that he spent six months in Osaka. This time, when he returned to China, he passed through the Northeast, Pingjin, Qinglu, etc., for two months. The deepest feeling he had was that he saw the atmosphere of national crisis in Japan every day. The whole country of Japan, from top to bottom, is preparing for 1936. They are constantly shouting and working hard to overcome the national crisis. When he returned to the country, he felt that the Chinese people were indifferent and forgot about it, and there was no atmosphere of national crisis at all. The Pingjin area was bustling with activity, eating, drinking, whoring, and gambling, just like usual. Japan is an aggressor country, and the government and people are working very hard. China is a country invaded, but it is as calm as usual. This is the most heartbreaking thing.

Young Military Officers The young military officer faction is very powerful on the Japanese political stage. The current Army Minister Araki is the leader of the young military officer faction. The reason for the formation of the young military officer faction is the reform of the conscription law. In the past, the conscription system required all citizens to serve in the military for two years. Now, workers and farmers still serve in the military for two years. Middle school students enter the Youth Training Corps while in school and receive strict military training, the same as regular soldiers. After entering university, they do not receive military training, but after graduation, they work as volunteer soldiers for one year. These university graduates have received long-term training in middle and primary schools, so they no longer serve as soldiers. At a minimum, they are awarded the rank of lieutenant. The best of the volunteer soldiers are selected and sent to the Army University for further study. Therefore, the students of the Army University are all outstanding university graduates who are not only good at military affairs, but also have rich knowledge of politics, economics, and society. Therefore, the minds of today's soldiers are no longer as simple as those of the old soldiers in the past. However, at a time when the economic organization of Japanese capitalism has reached its completion and consolidation, these soldiers have no place to use their force to develop their power, so they pretended to take leave and occupied the Northeast on September 18. Today, the young military officer faction is working hard to build a new force based on Manchuria. In terms of economic organization, they have completely abandoned the existing system in Japan and adhere to the unified control. The future results are unknown, but the Chinese people cannot fail to understand its causes and trends.

Controlled Economy When in Japan, there are emergency calls, speeches, broadcasts, and newspaper articles advocating emergency preparedness, such as finance, diplomacy, national defense, etc., almost every day. In addition to advocating, they are also actually proceeding every day. Although some Chinese newspapers also have articles on the crisis of 1936, there is nothing else besides this. For example, there are also people in our country who discuss the controlled economy, but it is only discussed and there is absolutely no possibility of implementation. In Japan, the government's control over enterprises, such as managing foreign exchange and limiting the establishment of bank branches, is implemented one by one. Mitsui Bank and others also deeply feel the government's oppression. Recently, due to the impending war between Japan and the United States and Japan and Russia, they have entered the wartime management period.

External and Internal When it comes to Japan's finances, it is also the same as robbing Peter to pay Paul. Its difficulties may be even worse than ours, but what is very different from us is that our military and politicians often use foreign issues to engage in internal disputes, while in other countries, foreign affairs are critical, which is precisely to coordinate internally and eliminate private opinions. This is the most heartbreaking and uncontrollable thing for us. Next, he stated that the psychology of fear and contempt should not be kept, etc.

Now that the government has organized a National Economic Committee to plan the control of various industries, the people should rise up to help together. Production and sales cooperation is especially not to be delayed. You, sir, have been leading the merchants for a long time and have been admired for your patriotism and love for the people. We hope to exert the strength of one word and nine tripods and gather the voice of ten thousand mountains echoing, to work for the country and plant benefits for the people. We will certainly be happy to support it. Now we transfer the declaration plan and the letter of undertaking, each one. In addition to filling it out and sending it first, we also ask you to widely solicit comrades and give us advice at any time. Looking at the clouds and mountains from afar, we cannot express all our desires."

Wu Huanru Talks About Organizing Food Production and Sales Institutions 125

Chairman Chiang believes that regulating food is of great importance to people's livelihood. Therefore, last month, he convened representatives from eight provinces and cities at the Nanchang Headquarters to hold a food conference. The municipal government sent Wu Huanru, the second section chief of the Social Affairs Bureau, and Gu Xin'yi, the chairman of the Food Industry Association, to participate. The results of the conference were very good. The most important things were the organization of food production and sales institutions and the establishment of food storage facilities. After Wu and Gu returned to Shanghai, they actively planned and proceeded to implement them as soon as possible. A reporter from the Central News Agency met with Wu Huanru yesterday morning. According to him, the recent progress is as follows:

Production and Sales Institutions Will Be Realized Soon 126

According to Wu, the importance of regulating food has been recognized by the people of the country. The current sharp drop in the price of domestic rice is the biggest cause of the bankruptcy of the agricultural economy. Although this city is the main market for selling rice, the inconvenience of inland rice transportation makes it difficult to collect large quantities of rice at one time. Therefore, general merchants often buy foreign rice. At the food conference convened by Chairman Chiang at the Nanchang Headquarters, the representative of this city proposed a plan to organize rice production and sales institutions, intending to ask Chairman Chiang to consult with the government to designate a bank to overdraw 1 million yuan in cash, and then raise 1 million yuan in cash from political and business circles to buy rice in Hunan, Jiangxi and other places. On the one hand, the price of inland rice is raised to save the decline of the rural economy, and on the other hand, foreign rice is resisted, so as to block the loopholes. However, the collection of inland rice to urban areas can be sold in part in this city, and can also be transported to Guangzhou, Tianjin and other places. Guangzhou and Tianjin import a large amount of foreign rice every year. If there is domestic rice to supply, then foreign rice can reduce imports, and the government can implement a full collection of foreign rice tax. The price of domestic rice is cheaper, and sales can be increased. However, the production and sales institutions will be handled by merchants, and the government will supervise them and maintain their permanence. The outline of the plan can be approved by Chairman Chiang to the representatives soon, and the representatives have already had considerable contact in Jiangxi, so the implementation period will not be far away.

Grain Storage Measures Have Not Yet Been Determined 127

Wu also talked about the warehouse problem, saying that this city had discussed this matter before, but it could not be realized due to limited funds. Recently, the central government has issued an order to all provinces and cities to store rice, for three reasons: (1) to regulate rice prices; (2) to prevent disaster years; (3) to deal with international changes. The method is that the county stores 10,000 stone, and the township stores 5,000 stone. As far as this city is concerned, the population is large, and the monthly demand for rice is about 100,000 stone, while the funds under the city's warehouses are only more than 200,000 yuan of real estate, and it is jointly owned with Jiangsu Province, so the number is not enough. Now, this city advocates preparing cash, because if there is cash, it is not difficult to buy rice in this city, and the land price in this city is expensive. If warehouses are established, a large amount of stacking land is required, and the cost of purchasing land is required in advance, which feels too uneconomical. Others advocate still following the central government's method to store rice, so this matter still needs to be discussed before a decision can be made.

Chen Jiliang Reviewed Various Land-Based Agencies Yesterday 128

Chen Jiliang, Political Vice Minister of the Navy and Chairman of the Review Committee, was originally scheduled to review the Tongji and Shun Sheng ships yesterday. However, due to changes in the program, he reviewed the Navy's Aircraft Manufacturing Department and the Jiangnan Shipyard in the morning, and the Navy Hospital and the Seamen's Training Institute in the afternoon. He is scheduled to review the Hydrographic Bureau and the Pilot Training Institute today.

International Issues Research Association Invites Chen Binhe to Lecture on the Russo-Japanese Problem 129

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, the situation between Japan and Russia has become increasingly tense recently, which is of great importance to our country's interests. The International Issues Research Association held a membership lecture at the Bank Club at 5:00 PM yesterday, and invited Chen Binhe, a member of the association, to lecture on "The Russo-Japanese Problem." The lecture was very long, and its outline was divided into ten items: (1) Diplomatic relations between Japan and the Soviet Union after September 18; (2) Japan's anti-Soviet remarks; (3) The necessity of the Russo-Japanese War; (4) The relationship between the Soviet Union and Manchuria; (5) Japan's preparations in Manchuria; (6) The Soviet leaders' remarks on national defense; (7) The Soviet Union's preparations in the Far East border; (8) A comparison of the national strength of Japan and the Soviet Union; (9) The Soviet army's combat plan in the eyes of the Japanese; (10) The Japanese prediction of the victory or defeat of the two countries in the eyes of the Japanese.

The Ministry of Communications Instructs Shipping Crew Members to Apply for Examination Within the Time Limit. Those Who Have Not Passed the Examination Are Not Allowed to Serve on Ships 130

The Ministry of Communications believes that the safety of passengers depends on the ocean navigation of ships, and the experience and knowledge of crew members are particularly important. Therefore, it held an examination in Beijing on the 24th of last month. However, due to business relations, there are still many people who have not been able to take the examination. Therefore, this special instruction is issued to various shipping companies and institutions: those who have not passed the examination are not allowed to serve on ships. The instructions are recorded as follows: "According to Article 16 of the Provisional Regulations on Crew Member Examination, 'Foreigners who are currently serving as officers of Chinese ships, regardless of whether they have obtained a merchant ship officer's certificate, shall, within six months from the date of implementation of these regulations, apply for examination and obtain a certificate in accordance with Article 1 of these regulations and the Provisional Regulations on Crew Member Certificates before they can serve.' Article 1 of the Detailed Rules for the Implementation of the Provisional Regulations on Crew Member Examination stipulates that 'All Chinese crew members currently serving on Chinese ships who have not obtained a merchant ship officer's certificate shall apply for examination within six months from the date of implementation of the Provisional Regulations on Crew Member Examination.' The regulations have been in effect since June 1st of this year, and more than five months have passed. The deadline for examination is approaching soon. All Chinese crew members currently serving on Chinese ships who have not obtained a certificate, and foreign crew members who have obtained or have not obtained a certificate, are all required to come to the Ministry before December 1st to apply for examination in order to comply with the laws. In addition to separate orders, the association is hereby ordered to forward this order to all crew members to comply with it. This order."

Reactions to the Increased Rent for Warehouses of the Beijing-Shanghai Railway Administration 131

The Beijing-Shanghai Railway Administration has changed its rental method, shortened the term, and increased the rent due to the difficulty of clearing up the stockpiled goods in the warehouse. It is now heard that the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce has received a letter from the Bengbu Miscellaneous Grain Industry Association, asking for efforts to cancel the increase and maintain the old rules. The original telegram to the Ministry of Railways is as follows: "To the Nanjing Ministry of Railways, the Beijing-Shanghai Railway is now revising the new rules for goods arriving at the Shanghai station. The rental period, which used to be seven days, is now changed to five days. The warehouse rent, which used to be 1.5 cents per ton, is now 5 cents, a sudden increase of almost three times, and the time limit is also shortened. This is a major blow to merchants. The intention of the Railway Administration is to restrict the accumulation of goods in the warehouse by raising the warehouse rent, and to promote rapid sales to avoid stagnation. This is only a one-sided idea of the Railway Administration, and it fails to take into account the difficulties of merchants. The goods of the merchants arriving in Shanghai must be sold wholesale. The more quickly they want to sell, the more difficult it is to get a good price. If the warehouse rent is too high, there is no room for waiting for a better price. A slight mistake will result in a loss. This will make miscellaneous grain merchants hesitate or even change to Changshu to save costs. This is not only inconvenient for merchants, but also will greatly affect the revenue of the Tianjin-Pukou and Beijing-Shanghai Railways. This kind of change by the Shanghai Railway Administration is like seeking fish in a dried-up well, and it will backfire. If you want to fundamentally solve the problem, you can only expand the warehouse to provide relief. How can you compare it to the rent of houses in the market and speculate on price increases? The merchants are concerned about their own interests, so they dare to appeal to you. Please, your Ministry, review and verify, and quickly order the Beijing-Shanghai Railway Administration to immediately cancel the new rules and continue to use the old system to emphasize railway policy and care for the difficulties of merchants. We are extremely anxious to await orders." (The following is omitted)

Turmoil Occurs on the Dachung Company's Da Fu Ship. Crew Members Demand Payment of Overdue Wages. The Social Affairs Bureau Has Scheduled Mediation for the 18th 132

According to the Xin Sheng News Agency, the Dachung Shipping Company at 282 Wai Ma Lu in Nanshi purchased the new Ning ship, renamed it the Da Fu ship, and prepared to operate the Shanghai-Yangzhou route. The manager, Wang Zhenxiang, hired 31 people, including Yang Tingsheng, the head of the watermen, and Zhang Xiang'an, the old helmsman, on June 21st of this year, with a monthly salary of 864 yuan. The ship was moored on the Huangpu River near the Longhua Airport. All the crew members stopped eating and jointly demanded payment from the manager, Wang Zhenxiang, because the sailing date was uncertain and the wages were delayed. They received a check for 300 yuan on October 13th and a check for 600 yuan on October 20th. When the due date arrived, the manager avoided meeting them, and the checks were returned by the bank. They went to demand payment again the other day, and were reported and detained by the Avenue Joffre Police Station. Fortunately, they were released on the spot after being questioned by the police chief. All the crew members reported to the Social Affairs Bureau and the Municipal Party Department for assistance. In addition to sending staff to investigate, the Social Affairs Bureau strictly ordered the manager, Wang Zhenxiang, to arrive at the bureau on time at 9:00 AM yesterday for questioning. When the time arrived, the manager of the company refused to attend, only sending a representative, so mediation was impossible. It is heard that the Social Affairs Bureau has scheduled a formal mediation according to law at 9:00 AM on the 18th.

The Yellow River Disaster Relief Association Ships Cotton Clothes to the Disaster Area and Distributes Donations from Various Provinces 133

This year's Yellow River flood has hit Hebei, Shandong, and Henan the hardest. In addition to providing emergency relief, the government has allocated funds to set up a Yellow River Disaster Relief Association to handle relief grain and clothing. Relief grain is purchased locally according to the principle of purchasing from neighboring harvest areas in the disaster area. Relief clothing is made in Shanghai, with 100,000 sets of cotton clothes distributed to disaster victims to keep them warm. The cotton clothes, along with 500 sets donated by Mrs. Tang Muchao of Beiping and 1,000 sets donated by Director Zeng Rongpu of the association, were all shipped to the disaster area on the 14th of this month. It is heard that Ms. Fang, the wife of Xi Dejiong, of the disaster relief group of the association, also specially donated 100 sets of new cotton clothes. Ms. Lu, the wife of Gao Dajing, the director of the transportation group, raised 200 sets from relatives and friends, which were also shipped to the disaster area together. However, the disaster area is vast and the number of disaster victims is large. Now it is winter, and the cold wind is piercing. But if you can get one more set of cotton clothes, you can save one more life. The association hopes that compatriots across the country will embrace the heart of compassion and generously donate to save the disaster victims.

In addition, the association has repeatedly received reports from the three provinces on the use of allocated funds. The approximate amounts are excerpted as follows: (Shandong) 8,000 yuan each for Shou Zhang, Yanggu, Dongping, Fanxian, Puxian, and Heze; 7,000 yuan for Juye; 5,000 yuan for Dong'e; 4,000 yuan each for Shanxian, Juancheng, and Jiaxiang; 3,000 yuan for Jining; 2,000 yuan for Wenshang; 1,000 yuan each for Jinxiang and Yutai, totaling 79,000 yuan. (Hebei) The first batch of 20,000 yuan has been allocated to Changyuan 8,000 yuan, Puyang Dongming 6,000 yuan each; the second batch of 30,000 yuan has also been remitted. (Henan) 40,000 yuan for Huaxian; 10,000 yuan for Lanfeng; 8,000 yuan for Kaocheng; 6,500 yuan each for Wuzhi and Fengqiu; 4,000 yuan for Wenxian; 1,000 yuan each for Mengjin, Kaifeng, and Mengxian; 500 yuan each for Sishui, Minquan, Yucheng, Guangwu, Zhongmou, and Gongxian.

The Zhang River Disaster Is Equal to the Yellow River Disaster. Representatives of Linzhang County Send a Letter Requesting Relief 134

The Shanghai Charity Organizations Yellow River Emergency Relief Association received a letter yesterday from more than 20 representatives of Linzhang County, Henan, including Du Xian, stating the disaster situation in the county and requesting equal treatment, without discrimination, and providing relief. The letter stated, "To Chairman Xu of the United Association of Shanghai Charity Organizations for Yellow River Emergency Relief, we have learned that the Zhang River in Linzhang County was first seen in the Shangshu Yugong, named Hengzhang. The so-called Heng means horizontal, implying the meaning of collapse and horizontal flow. The Zhang River has been prone to flooding since ancient times. Moreover, the river channel is wide and the water is fierce, often causing sudden and violent floods, sometimes reaching tens of miles wide. Anyang and Neihuang counties in Henan, as well as Daming County in Hebei, have all been affected, but Linzhang is the first to bear the brunt, and the damage is particularly severe. Among the rivers in Henan, besides the Yellow River, the Zhang River in Linzhang is the most severe. Therefore, there is a saying that it is a small Yellow River. Since June of the 22nd year of the Republic of China (1933), the Zhang River has flooded 20 times, with breaches in several places, submerging more than 100 villages. Chairman Liu of the Henan Provincial Government appealed to neighboring provinces, describing the Zhang River as the first to mention in the Henan flood. Its turbulent waves, floods, submergence of wheat, collapse of the bank, collapse of houses, drowning of the population, and the drifting of all livestock and items are all tragic scenes that are heartbreaking to see and talk about in Shanghai. The disaster victims have no place to live or eat, and they are displaced. The damage is equal to that of the Yellow River. Your Excellency is a dragon gate of this generation, with great achievements and high reputation. We are all human beings, and we care about hunger and drowning. We implore you to treat everyone equally, without discrimination, and in addition to raising funds for the Yellow River emergency relief, also raise funds for the Zhang River emergency relief. May your kindness be extended and your merits accumulate and grow. We also ask you to quickly allocate relief funds to extend the lives of the hundreds of thousands of hungry disaster victims and to reverse the disaster. The more than 100 riverside villages of the disaster victims in Linzhang, Henan, represented by Du Xian and more than 20 others, send a true telegram."

Recent News from the Pudong Zhanghua Woolen Mill; Discarding Steam Engine; Switching to Electric Power Operation 141

The Zhanghua Woolen Mill in Zhoujiadu, Pudong, is a large-scale factory that weaves various wool flannels and gabardines at reasonable prices and high quality. Therefore, Chinese people are eagerly buying and using these products, resulting in excellent sales. The factory originally had a 240-horsepower steam engine for power needs. However, due to its small capacity and excessive coal consumption, it has been discarded. Instead, ten electric motors have been purchased, totaling 254 horsepower, for operation. The China United Engineering Company was commissioned to install them, and the Pudong Electric Company installed power lines, including a 400 kVA transformer. Power supply was connected on the 11th of this month. It is said that the electricity price is quite low, which can save a lot of expenses every month. Furthermore, the Pudong Electric Company has an ample supply of electricity, allowing for easy expansion and supply. In the future, the factory's products will be more exquisite due to the uniform speed of the electric motors. The selling price will gradually decrease as the cost decreases. This is truly good news for the national goods industry.

County Agricultural Education Center to Hold Ox Plowing Competition Tomorrow; Opening Ceremony in the Morning, Judging in the Afternoon; Chairman Chiang Kai-shek Also Sends Encouraging Words to the Event 143

The Shanghai County Farmers' Education Center will hold its fifth ox plowing competition on the 17th of this month in Zhuanqiao, on the Hu-Min Road. The details are as follows:

Opening Tomorrow: The opening ceremony will be held at 10:00 AM tomorrow at the Farmers' Lecture Hall. The ceremony will include everyone standing at attention, singing the Party song, paying the highest respect to the Party and national flags and the portrait of Sun Yat-sen, the chairman respectfully reading Sun Yat-sen's will, a moment of silence, the chairman delivering the opening speech, representatives of various organizations providing guidance and speeches, shouting slogans, and the completion of the ceremony. Judging will take place in the afternoon.

Judging Criteria: (1) General Overview: divided into weight, body type, physique, movement, temperament, and physical condition. (2) Head and Neck: divided into head, forehead, eyes, ears, horns, lips, jaw, and neck. (3) Forequarters: divided into shoulder, elbow, forearm, knee, shin, hock, fetlock, and hoof. (4) Midsection: divided into chest, ribs, back, waist, and abdomen. (5) Hindquarters: divided into hip bones, rump, femur, stifle, gaskin, hock, fetlock, and hoof.

Shanghai-Nanjing Railway Stations to Develop Small Gardens; Not Only Beautifying the Environment but Also Benefiting Hygiene 144

Respectfully, the Shanghai Charity Groups Joint Association for Raising Funds for the Yellow River Flood Relief, commissioned by Chairman Xu Shiying and Vice Chairmen Wang Zhen and Wang Xiaolai, November 15."

Haikjingbo Circus Discovers Counterfeit Tickets; A Conspiracy Between Two Ticket Sellers and a Postal Worker; Approached a Printing Shop to Imitate Tickets Daily; Profited Hundreds of Gold Each Over Several Days 151

The Haikjingbo Circus recently came to Shanghai from overseas and established a circus arena at the original site of the Dahua Hotel on Jing'an Temple Road. Since its opening, it has been a sensation in China, with unprecedented business success. Li Zhongyun, a Ningbo native, and Wang Guangrong, a Zhenjiang native, were hired as ticket sellers when the circus opened. Li worked the day shift, and Wang worked the night shift. They have been serving diligently for more than a month. However, in the past week, Li and Wang suddenly had bad intentions. Seeing the circus's

Thriving Business, 152

they had a strange idea and wanted to profit from it. They discussed the matter with Ren Linxiang, a Ningbo native who worked as a postal worker No. 618 at the Post Office, and decided to jointly forge admission tickets, divided into one-yuan and two-yuan tickets. Their plan was quite meticulous. First, Ren contacted Li Liu, the owner of the Fuxing Printing Shop at No. 1303, Zhonghua Road, Nanshi, and Yao Jiqing, a printing apprentice, and arranged for them to print more than a hundred counterfeit tickets every day, paying a commission of 18 yuan, with Li Liu receiving 15 yuan and Yao receiving 3 yuan. Since the circus tickets changed daily and had different colors, Ren was asked to go to a Western trading company on Nanjing Road the next afternoon to buy one of each, a two-yuan and a one-yuan ticket, and take them to the Fuxing Printing Shop to print imitations overnight. The next morning, Ren would take the printed counterfeit tickets to the circus and hand them over to Li and Wang.

Sold in Secret 153

This plan was put into effect on the 8th of this month. However, because the counterfeit tickets printed were of poor quality, they did not dare to sell them rashly. It was not until the 10th of this month that they reprinted them and began to sell them in secret. This has been going on for five days, and the profits have been substantial. Every day, after deducting the printing fee of 18 yuan from the proceeds of the counterfeit tickets, the remainder was divided equally among Li, Wang, and Ren. Each person could earn 40 to 50 yuan per day. Therefore, in the past few days, the three of them have each received about 210 yuan. However, this kind of trickery could only last for a while. When the circus reopened for the second time at 9:15 on the 14th,

Thousands of Spectators 154

flooded in like a tide, buying tickets and entering. A ticket collector suddenly noticed that the one-yuan and two-yuan ticket stubs had uneven paper thickness. Upon closer inspection, he realized that they were counterfeit. He reported this to the circus secretary and accountant, Mr. Huike Na, who questioned the audience about where they bought their tickets. They all replied that they bought them at the ticket booth at the entrance. He then reported this to the Western police officer stationed at the site and telegraphed the Jing'an Temple Police Station, sending Chinese detectives Wang Yongjun and Bao Zhu Shanghe to the ticket booth to arrest the two ticket sellers, Li and Wang. 250 yuan in cash was found on Li's body, 40 yuan was found on Wang's body, as well as 28 counterfeit tickets, two blank sheets of paper, an ink box, and two stamps. They were taken to the police station and confessed that their accomplice, Ren Linxiang, was hiding in Room 120 of the Shenzhou Hotel on Zhejiang Road. They then went and apprehended Ren. Ren confessed that the counterfeit tickets were printed at the Fuxing Printing Shop. That night, the Chinese and Western detectives went to Zhonghua Road with detectives from the Public Security Bureau and arrested Li Liu, the owner of the shop, and Yao Jiqing, the apprentice. They seized

Four Printing Plates, 155

200 yuan in cash, and a sample of the counterfeit ticket from the 15th. They were taken to the Public Security Bureau for detention and will be transferred after official procedures are completed. Yesterday morning, the police, along with the witnesses, escorted Li, Wang, and Ren to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Police lawyer Wang Yaotang, in addition to recounting the above situation in detail, stated that Li and Wang are now being prosecuted for breach of trust under Article 366 of the Criminal Code, and Ren is being prosecuted for fraud under Article 363 of the Criminal Code. However, Li Liu, the owner of the Fuxing Printing Shop, and Yao Jiqing, the apprentice, as well as the evidence, are still detained in the Public Security Bureau. He requested the court to issue an official document to the police station to facilitate the transfer. Mr. Huike Na, the representative of the Haikjingbo Circus, stated that at 9:15 last night, he received a report from a ticket collector that the one-yuan and two-yuan tickets were

Of Different Thicknesses 156

and of inferior quality. Upon careful inspection, I realized that they were counterfeit. I questioned them and found out that they were sold by ticket seller No. 2, so I reported it to the police officer. Spectator Ma Xiupu testified that he went to the circus at 3:00 PM on the 14th to buy four one-yuan tickets and went to see the circus with four friends that evening. The ticket collector said that the tickets were fake. I was unaware. I then went to the police station with a letter of guarantee. Spectator Shen Jinxia testified that he bought two one-yuan tickets and two six-jiao tickets last night, which were also fake. Upon questioning, Li Zhongyun confessed, "I was hired as a ticket seller at the circus with Wang when it opened. These counterfeit tickets were first

Started on the 10th 157

in collusion with Wang and Ren Linxiang for about four days. I earned 210 yuan in total." Wang Guangrong said, "The 40 yuan taken from me was earned yesterday. I did not participate in this at first. It was a conspiracy between Li and Ren. Two days later, I discovered the secret and also earned 115 yuan." Ren Linxiang also admitted to the accusation, stating that he discussed it with Li and Wang, and went to a Western trading company to buy real tickets and took them to the Fuxing Printing Shop for printing. He confessed that he had earned 150 to 160 yuan, which he had used to buy clothes. After verifying the confessions, Judge Wu Tingying ordered the three defendants to be returned to custody, pending further investigation and questioning in seven days.

Chaos on the Jianghua Steamer Passing Xunyang; Ticket Inspection by the Purser... A Hawker Falls into the Water; A Brawl When the Ship Passes Jiujiang 158

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Yangtze River steamer, the Jianghua, encountered a series of incidents on its return voyage from Hankou to Shanghai, including a hawker falling into the water upstream from Jiujiang and a large group of hawkers causing trouble in Jiujiang, resulting in the ship's crew being assaulted. The Jianghua has now arrived in Shanghai, and the details of these incidents are as follows:

Hawkers Refuse to Purchase Tickets 159

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's model steamer on the Yangtze River route, the Jianghua, loaded passengers and cargo in Hankou and sailed downstream back to Shanghai. Many passengers boarded in Hankou. As usual, it was necessary to check passenger tickets near Wuxue to prevent unauthorized boarding. The purser, Mr. Wang, checked the tickets one by one. On the outer platform of the upper deck, he found a passenger who had not purchased a ticket and had混入the ship. As usual, the purser asked him to buy a ticket, but the passenger claimed to be a hawker selling food and insisted on not buying a ticket, leading to an argument.

Suddenly Falls into the Water During the Argument 160

At that time, the purser, Mr. Wang, and a steward named Tang Sheng said, "Since you are a hawker, you should show the goods you are selling." The passenger then took out a bamboo basket from the cabin, containing two baked cakes. The purser said, "Since you are a hawker, why don't you have any food? You are obviously pretending." The steward Tang Sheng suddenly snatched the basket from the passenger. In the ensuing chaos, the hawker and the steward became entangled. Later, the hawker and the bamboo basket somehow fell into the Yangtze River from the Jianghua. After the hawker fell into the water, the business manager immediately ordered the ship to stop and lower a sampan to search, but there was no trace of him.

Major Dispute in Jiujiang 161

The Jianghua continued to Jiujiang as usual. According to the crew members on the upper deck, a small boat rescued the hawker after he fell into the water, and the matter seemed to be over. However, when the Jianghua arrived at the Jiujiang dock, a group of more than 200 hawkers gathered and boarded the ship to question the purser about why they had pushed the hawker into the Yangtze River, causing him to be in danger. About 60 hawkers boarded the ship, while more than 200 people were at the dock to provide support. An argument broke out, and a major brawl ensued.

Several Crew Members Injured 162

The hawkers came specifically to cause trouble and retaliate. About five of those who boarded the ship appeared to be leaders. As soon as a fight broke out, they assaulted anyone they encountered. Among the crew members who were injured were Chief Officer Chen, Purser Wang, and several stewards. Some had head injuries, some had body injuries, and some had injuries to their hands and feet. The hawkers also damaged many items in the purser's office. Fortunately, the military police on board intervened to stop the fighting, otherwise the situation would have been even worse.

Ship Plate and Mailbox Seized 163

During the melee, the hawkers broke into the purser's office, vandalized objects, and even seized the ship's plate and mailbox, preventing the Jianghua from sailing. After this incident, the hawkers first reported to the local Public Security Bureau and the Garrison Headquarters, claiming that the Jianghua had pushed someone into the water. Therefore, after the incident, the Garrison Headquarters sent troops on board to investigate the truth. The crew members reported the incident.

Investigation of Troublemakers 164

During the assault, five leading hawkers were detained by the military police on the Jianghua. Later, the Jiujiang Garrison Headquarters sent personnel to the ship and took the five men away to the Public Security Bureau for questioning. As for the steward Tang Sheng, the hawkers claimed that he was the one who pushed the person into the water, so personnel from the Garrison Headquarters also took him away to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation. The ship plate and mailbox were returned by the Public Security Bureau, and the ship was then able to set sail for Shanghai.

Manager Reports to Shanghai 165

The Jianghua arrived in Shanghai yesterday, and the business manager immediately went to the head office to report the incident to the department heads. He stated that the hawkers would likely seek revenge when the Jianghua passed Xunyang on its upstream voyage, which could lead to a major incident. He requested the company to telegraph the central government and ask the local military police to provide protection. As for the person who was pushed into the water, the Xunyang Public Security Bureau will interrogate the steward to clarify the matter. How the hawkers who committed the assault will be punished is still unknown.

Page 13

Joint Meeting of Nanshi Winter Defense and Security Police and Community Leaders; Organization of the Shanghai South District Winter Defense Joint Association; Police and Community Leaders Jointly Responsible for Protecting Security 166

Regarding the Nanshi winter defense security issue, with the winter defense period approaching rapidly, it is extremely appropriate to pay attention to preparedness. Guan Yun, the district chief of the First District of the Nanshi Public Security Bureau, specifically joined with Li Jing, the district chief of the Second District, yesterday afternoon to incite the Nanshi Security Corps and gentlemen and merchants from all walks of life to discuss this year's Nanshi winter defense security measures and methods. The "Fuxing She" reporter Zixingshen was in attendance and noted the details, which are divided below:

Attendees: Guan Yun, district chief of the First District; Li Jing, district chief of the Second District; Yi Jiren, head of the First Station of the First District; Liu Yunfang, head of the Second Station of the First District; Jin Dianyang, head of the Third Station of the First District; Shen Jianhua, head of the First Station of the Second District; Tang Jinghui, head of the Second Station of the Second District; Wang Zhuangfei, of the Security Corps; Mao Zijian, of the United Fire Brigade; Yu (various names), team leader of the First Team of the Security Corps; Zeng Ze, team leader of the Second Team; Gu Jiuru (proxy), team leader of the Fourth Team; Zhu Dansheng, team leader of the Third Team; Wang Guixin, deputy team leader of the Ninth Team; and over a hundred others.

Report on the Purpose: At the opening of the meeting, Guan Yun, the district chief of the First District and the chair, reported the purpose of the meeting, stating that the area of Nanshi is usually a lively place and it is now the winter defense season, so the police, the Security Corps, merchants and residents should cooperate closely to jointly take responsibility for protecting security. Next, Li Jing, the district chief of the Second District, delivered a speech, saying that it is a necessary event for the police and the Security Corps to jointly manage the winter defense. With the organization of the Security Corps, the local citizens and masses are more familiar with the local situation than the police. With this joint management of the winter defense, there is no cause for concern about the security of Nanshi.

Cases Resolved: Tang Jinghui proposed that the inspection of automobiles should be accompanied by the inspection of judicial licenses, which was resolved and passed. Li Jing proposed that with the winter defense approaching, all unemployed vagrants within the area should be driven away or detained, and iron gates should be added to the openings of each lane, which was resolved to be handled jointly with local citizens. Wang Zhuangfei proposed that when the Security Corps captures criminals and sends them to the police station, the police station should immediately give a reply, which was resolved and passed. Mao Zijian proposed that in the event of a fire, police officers at the scene of the fire should drive the idle people away from the scene of the fire to 300 feet away, so that the fire brigade and firefighters can act, which was resolved and passed. Guan Gong proposed that a winter defense joint association should be organized by the merchants of each door, which was resolved to have district chief Guan and district chief Li present a petition to the Public Security Bureau for approval.

Preparatory Committee: To prepare for the Nanshi Beach Merchants Winter Defense Joint Association, a 23-member preparatory committee was appointed on the spot: Guan Yun, Li Jing, Gao Ziyun, Li Yingsheng, Mao Zijian, He Yongshou, Wu Qinzhi, Ma Ziliang, Gao Jianji, Zhou Jingzhai, Zhu Sanxian, Gong Ziyan, Pan Xusheng, Huang Shixiang, Li Chenxiang, Wang Jiting, Yao Qilian, Li Bohong, Wang Zhuangfei, Gu Guyi, Gu Bojin, and Zhou Deqing, and it was decided to convene the first meeting of the Preparatory Committee on Saturday afternoon.

Yousheng Travel Group Seeks New Members 171
