The Importance of Leading by Example for Elementary School Teachers 251

— Hu Qinwen

Shanghai has a plethora of elementary schools. If you're willing to wander around, you'll see those blue signs with white characters for "○○ Elementary School" everywhere. They're truly eye-catching, so many that you can't count or remember them all.

This is a good phenomenon, because the development of children's education can nurture countless good citizens. A weak country can rely on it to become strong, and an impoverished people can rely on it to become rich. However, to educate children, there must be good teachers, and only then can children be cultivated. For example, a piece of jade in the rough, if the carving skills are exquisite, then the jade can become a valuable treasure. But if the skills are not good and one haphazardly wields the knife, then a good piece of jade will surely be ruined to the point of being worthless!

Promoting domestic goods is the duty of every citizen! And elementary school teachers, in particular, must recognize that they are citizens of this country. What they eat, wear, and use must be domestic goods. Then, the children will see this and naturally imitate them. The sales of domestic goods can increase as a result, and the country's economic difficulties can be eased. If those teachers disregard the country and the children, as described in the "Dream of the Red Chamber," with their hearts "blinded by lard," they must wear foreign goods and use imported goods. When the children see this, they will imitate them, developing habits of vanity and superficiality. Then, what we educators have created is nothing more than some "little foreign slaves"! There is nothing more harmful to the country and the people than this!

Confucius said: "Correct yourself before you correct others!" I hope that those educators will all lead by example, because children's ability to imitate is very strong. One who stays near vermilion gets stained red, and one who stays near ink gets stained black. The future of domestic goods is truly based on this!

Contributing Opinions

Two Small Suggestions 252

— Huang Xuanwan

In this year of promoting domestic goods, we have indeed sung loudly and earnestly discussed the issue of how to promote domestic goods and resist imported goods. If we could all diligently follow through, then we might say that we have reached a considerable stage. However, on the other hand, we must also turn around and look at our own domestic goods factories – how is the progress in manufacturing? Has there been a reasonable increase in productivity? Has it been possible to achieve a considerable reduction in costs? What about improvements in products and lower prices?

Everyone knows that now is the most critical transition period for our country's domestic goods industry. "The sleeping lion of the East has awakened!" The revitalization of the domestic goods industry is the prelude to its roar. Looking at the nationwide high tide of promoting domestic goods with one voice, the rapid progress of our domestic goods factories, striving for excellence, regarding the past external promotion and advertising propaganda, are necessary conditions for our budding new industries, then how to improve production, reduce costs, make products beautiful, adapt supply and demand, and promote industrial and commercial prosperity and rural revitalization, naturally is especially the most important goal. Now I have the following two issues, to seek practical solutions, and contribute some opinions:

1. Raw materials: Because our country is a country with backward production, raw materials are extremely scarce. The use of foreign raw materials by domestic goods factories has always been an undeniable fact. Now, to concretely solve this problem, we must try our best to use domestic raw materials. For those that already exist, we will vigorously promote them, and for those that do not exist, we will find ways to start them. Within a certain period, there should be a clear decrease in the importation of foreign raw materials. And this is also the way to relieve unemployed workers and peasants and revive the countryside.

2. Organization: The development of an enterprise naturally requires the perfection of internal organization. The business and manufacturing departments of domestic goods factories must first cooperate and collaborate. For example, taking an enamel factory as an example, its products include several major categories such as washbasins, cups, rice bowls, food baskets, and kerosene stoves. And under each category, there are still dozens of different colors and patterns. Therefore, in terms of sales, the relationship of timing, the so-called supply and demand distribution, all require strict statistics. A certain type of goods may be selling well right now, but a certain type of goods must have its style improved… issues like these must be addressed by establishing a Business Liaison Committee, composed of personnel from the business and manufacturing departments, or a special Business Investigation Department should be established to investigate the market situation, sales information, and intelligence in detail. Otherwise, if business and manufacturing are often isolated, it is possible that a certain product is waiting to be sold, but the warehouse is out of stock, or a certain product's sales are temporarily stagnant, but a large amount of goods are shipped out and accumulated, and other contradictory possibilities may occur. In the previous issue, Mr. Yang Yao talked about Mr. Xi Guansheng's high talent and great ability in managing mooncakes, which is naturally enough for us to follow.

In short, the domestic goods industry, which is expected by all, is still in its infancy. It is like a baby in swaddling clothes, still requiring the nanny to dutifully maintain it. If it waits until its own body is healthy, the masses support it, and "the roots are strong and the branches are flourishing," then its future will naturally be limitless!

Domestic Goods Cartoons

"Uphold the King and Expel the Barbarians" (國貨漫畫) 253

— Ning Ziqiang

Mr. Wang is an old licentiate from the Qing Dynasty. His aged appearance vividly portrays a kind and benevolent face. Because Mr. Wang has the appearance of a moralistic gentleman, people say that his thinking is outdated, calling him a pedant. Mr. Wang also gladly considers himself a pedant, without feeling offended by people's insults or expressing any resentment.

One day, Mr. Wang gave a speech about promoting domestic goods to the students. The opening statement was: "Uphold the King and Expel the Barbarians." The students were all stunned by the teacher, suspecting that Mr. Wang had inserted the nonsensical phrase "Uphold the King and Expel the Barbarians" into the middle of his speech about promoting domestic goods. Isn't this somewhat contrary to the current revolutionary trend? Isn't this 18th-century thinking? The students were at a loss, all looking at the teacher.

With great difficulty, after Mr. Wang's explanation, they finally understood that what Mr. Wang meant by upholding the king was upholding the king of domestic goods; what he meant by expelling the barbarians was resisting foreign goods. Only then did the students suddenly realize the truth.

Since this news spread to society, those who previously mistakenly thought that Mr. Wang's mind was dull have now changed their previous attitude of humiliation and contempt to one of respect and admiration. And from then on, everyone considered Mr. Wang to be a person whose thoughts were rooted in the old but whose thinking was new, not a complete old fossil.

Inventor

Inventing Paper Made from Rice Straw 254

— Jian Yin

In society, with the needs of the times, the utility of paper has become increasingly important. Among them, newspapers are the most important. According to customs statistics, the annual import of newsprint from abroad is no less than 30 million taels of customs silver. The great amount of leakage is increasing. In recent years, both the government and the public have been making great efforts to promote self-manufacturing. However, although newspapers have a wide range of uses, their value is very low. If there is no raw material with abundant production and low manufacturing costs, failures are inevitable. The raw material for newspapers in Western countries is made of wood, because they have many forests. Therefore, Chinese people often consider using other raw materials with relatively high yields to replace wood pulp. Because our country lacks forests and felling is not easy, recently, Du Shihua, the director of the Meili Paper Mill in Hangzhou, invented the manufacture of paper from rice straw. However, rice straw has always been used to make straw paper and cardboard and has no other use. Even if it is used to make paper, it is difficult to bleach and difficult to process due to its rough texture. Now, after Mr. Du's successful steaming experiment, it is indeed satisfactory. Although the paper produced is not as smooth as ordinary newspaper paper, it can be printed on both sides and will not bleed ink. As for the cost, it is one-third lower than wood pulp, about only 100 yuan per ton of pure white grass pulp. From this point of view, rice straw has become a raw material for newsprint. It is reported that Mr. Du is now preparing a large-scale factory to engage in production to meet social needs and has submitted an application to the provincial government to be forwarded to the Ministry of Industry for approval to grant a ten-year patent, which will recover a lot of rights and interests for the future of domestic goods.

One Who Has a Mind 255

(1) Preface

Nothing is difficult in the world for one who sets his mind to it. Newton thought of gravity from seeing apples, and Franklin understood electricity from flying a kite, which are examples. The achievements of many domestic goods inventors are not necessarily certain from the beginning. If readers do not believe it, there are real stories to prove it.

(2) Apprentice who invented the electric fan

Mr. Yang Jichuan, the apprentice of a cloth shop who invented the Huasheng electric fan, has not only achieved personal success but also has a valuable place in the history of domestic goods in China. It is said that Western electric fans have been hit hard, and Huasheng electric fans have even been sold abroad!

(3) Hu Xiyuan becomes a monk halfway

Mr. Hu Xiyuan, the owner of Yapu'er, did not start out in the light bulb industry. However, Yapu'er's own light bulb business failed, but when Hu Xiyuan came out, he achieved success and carried it forward, relying on a person who has a mind.

(4) The beginning of China's heavy industry

Wu Yun first said: "Now the mission of Tianchu is not only to engage in chemical light industry, I am determined to start engaging in the promotion of heavy industry."

(5) The development history of Sanyou

Sanyou Industrial Society originally made candle wicks in a small house at the intersection of North Sichuan Road. If it had not gone through a period of hard work, how could it have been resented by a certain country's ronin, and the Triangle brand became popular at home and abroad!

(6) The transformation of fried dough sticks can expand the grand plan

Boss Xi of Wanshengyuan said: "If you transform fried dough sticks so that they can be packed in brocade boxes for gift-giving, then you can make a lot of profit and greatly expand your grand plan!"

(7) The success of Tianxu Wo Sheng

Mr. Chen Diexian of the Family Industry Society was still struggling on the lakes in the early years of the Republic of China. Later, he went from being a traveling secretary to making a living by writing and selling articles until he achieved success. This happened over more than 20 years. (Yu Zhicheng)

Visiting Notes

Notes on Visiting the Shengsheng Ranch 256

— Gan Chunquan

The Shanghai Shengsheng Ranch, located at the intersection of Daxilu and Columbia Road, was initiated by Mr. Shen Jiucheng, the founder of the Sanyou Industrial Society. It has been in operation for four years. The equipment is clean, and the latest steam disinfection and cold air sterilization machines are used. The scale is large, the reputation is growing, and the number of customers is increasing. The reporter was very happy to see the actual situation of the ranch. Yesterday, I received an invitation from Mr. Guang and drove by car to the China Vocational Education Society to visit with gentlemen such as Yao Huiquan, He Qingjian, Pan Yangyao, and Yang Chonggao. The following is a record of Mr. Shen's speech and the general situation of the ranch:

(A) Mr. Shen's speech

The fresh milk business in Shanghai, including the large and small ranches run by foreigners, has an annual value of 3.6 million yuan. Among them, the ranches run by Chinese people have a total annual value of 1.2 million yuan, which is only one-third of the city's business. In addition to fresh milk, there are also two types of canned condensed milk and milk powder. According to the comparison, condensed milk and milk powder are easier to use, carry, and store, and the price is cheaper than fresh milk, so many people use them. In the whole of Shanghai, the total annual value of the three items of fresh milk, condensed milk, and milk powder is 33.6 million yuan, which is quite alarming. Mr. Shen saw that most of the milk business in Shanghai was in the hands of foreigners, and the rights and interests were overflowing, so he was determined to improve it. Mr. Shen's ambition was fully sympathized by his colleagues.

Mr. Shen said that to improve the milk business, we must first pay attention to raising cattle. Some advocate raising foreign breeds of cattle, and some advocate raising Chinese breeds of cattle. According to Mr. Shen's opinion, it is better to raise Chinese breeds of cattle. There are three reasons for this: (1) Chinese breeds of cattle, one cow, can collect 8 pounds of milk per day, which can be increased to 12 pounds after the first mating, and then 20 or more pounds. Now, it is planned to raise 100 proven cows and 10 bulls in the areas of Chuansha, Liuhe, and Danyang. After 17 years, the number will be reproduced to 700 heads. By analogy, after 20 years, the 23.6 million yuan of milk rights and interests in Shanghai can be entirely in the hands of Chinese people. (2) Raising Chinese breeds of cattle in more than three or five thousand heads. According to the Shanghai Concession regulations, each shed can raise 80 heads of cattle. With 5,000 heads, 625 sheds are needed. Where can such a large ranch come from? Even if there is, it cannot afford the burden. It should be raised in the city and part in the countryside. If it is raised in the countryside, the sales of milk will be more difficult. Therefore, it is necessary to cooperate between the countryside and the city, which will be of great benefit to the Chinese countryside. (3) The price of ordinary Chinese cattle is about 600 yuan per head, which is cheaper than foreign cattle. Now, if a Chinese cow produces 8 pounds of milk per day, each pound is calculated at 30 cents, and the capital can be repaid in more than seven months. In addition, the production of calves is an extra benefit, so it is beneficial to be raised separately by individual farmers or raised in a ranch.

To sum up, we should know that Chinese people should raise Chinese breeds of cattle, but to raise a large number of dairy cattle, capital must be sufficient, and management must be excellent. Therefore, the five aspects of ranch, bank, cooperative, technician, and veterinarian should cooperate to achieve great success.

(B) General situation of the ranch

The Shanghai Municipal Council's Hygiene Department considers the A-brand fresh milk to be the best. Currently, only four Chinese ranches have obtained this license: Shengsheng Ranch, Freedom Farm, Xuzhi Company, and Huade Farm. Each ranch produces about 2,000 pounds of milk per day. Now, Shengsheng Ranch has (1) a machine disinfection room. All items related to filling milk in this room must first be disinfected by scientific methods. (2) a high-pressure steam disinfection room. The milk is placed in a disinfection pot and high-pressure steam is passed in to eliminate all dirt. (3) a low-pressure disinfection room. The milk is placed in a low-pressure disinfection. The temperature is generally 145 degrees, and after 35 minutes, there is no need to use high temperature to disinfect, so there is not much change in the inherent components of milk. (4) milking shed. This is specially made and must be inspected by the Hygiene Department. (5) ranch is spacious and comfortable. (6) a cold air engine room, with careful layout. The ranch milks three times a day. The milkers disinfect their hands in advance. If the dairy cow is about to urinate or defecate during milking, another worker will pay attention and clean it up immediately, so that the milk will not be soiled at all. According to the regulations of the Municipal Council's Hygiene Department, the A-brand milk contains up to 30,000 bacteria, but after actual inspection, the milk from each farm contains only three or four hundred bacteria, which can make those who drink disinfected milk take it with peace of mind.

After the visit, Mr. Shen Jiucheng gave each person a bottle of fresh milk to taste on the spot, and everyone was very satisfied. Then, everyone immediately decided to order it and promote the quality. According to Mr. Shen, fresh milk should not be cooked in a metal pot. It is best to use a water bowl, fill it with warm water, put the milk bottle in it, heat it slightly, and drink it. It is the most hygienic. It should not be cooked too hot in a metal pot, which will lose its nutritional components. Those with weak bodies at home must drink domestic sterilized milk regularly, one to nourish their personal bodies, and one to recover national rights and interests. It is a win-win situation. Happy to record it.

Domestic Goods Anecdotes

The Decline of Signboards 257

— Zhi

The role of a signboard is like the clothing of a store, it has a sense of the times; in this era when the big wheel of time is moving forward, fashion is changing with each passing day, but there are also many signboards that are declining.

Why did the "Manchu Han Imperial Feast" in the restaurant have to be changed to "Great Han Imperial Feast"? Isn't this a manifestation of the success of the Xinhai Revolution?

After the opening of Shanghai, Guanghuo stores were transformed into foreign goods stores. The signboard was selling Eastern and Western goods. From urban areas to rural towns, they have done their best, presiding over the work of blood transfusion for many years. However, since the May Fourth Movement, under the pressure of public anger, everyone had to change their signboards, making the joke of Sino-Western goods.

Department stores can be said to be all-encompassing, and "managing global goods" is even more grand and imposing. However, in the year of domestic goods, this signboard will inevitably decline, I dare to guarantee.

Now, domestic goods companies have replaced department stores, and department stores have also added domestic goods markets or domestic goods shopping malls. Although the intention is to promote them, domestic goods are not despised by people, which is enough to prove it.

However, this has not yet completed the mission of the domestic goods movement! In any case, we have to smash the signboard of "managing global goods" so that there are only domestic goods stores in this society, not department stores!

Random Notes from the Bushu Studio 258

▲ Poor Loom

Old Man Zhang is one of the richest people in the village. Unfortunately, he has worked hard all his life and only has three daughters, without any sons. Those with thin mouths often chant "The royal family is originally a tile kiln." Fortunately, Old Man Zhang believes that men and women are equal and have the same right to inherit under the laws of the Republic of China, so he doesn't take it to heart.

Old Man Zhang's wife is also a scheming person. Seeing that her daughters were growing up and would always marry, she wove a few pieces of homespun cloth early and late to use as wedding dresses. After the eldest daughter got married, she also prepared to weave for the second and third daughters.

The autumn weather is cool, and the wedding day is coming soon. Old Man Zhang's eldest daughter is getting married. However, the eldest lady said to her mother: The cloth woven from soil is rough and ugly. How can I walk in front of people wearing it? I want to cut some foreign cloth to avoid being laughed at for being rustic.

Her mother agreed with this and said: Foreign cloth is cheap, and the colors and patterns are good-looking. You don't have to weave it yourself in the future! So she ordered the long-term worker to chop down the loom and burn it as firewood.

When the loom was chopped down, it seemed to be crying wuwuwu. At this time, Old Man Zhang had just returned from the teahouse. Seeing this scene, he felt both sad and angry, so he scolded his wife: I, Zhang, have today's position, all thanks to a loom and a hoe. What I eat and wear doesn't cost money to buy. Now that the loom has been chopped down, half of the family property has been spent by you! After saying that, he stroked the loom and cried bitterly.

At this time, the eldest lady and her mother also regretted it and cried together. It was a room full of joy, turned into a day of dark clouds, who taught you to be fascinated by foreign cloth and chop down this loyal servant-like loom!

Short Story Meeting

Ying's Awakening 260

— Xu Jiao Gong

Joy and excitement filled Ying's heart, and she felt very satisfied as she gazed at the new dress just sent from the tailor shop in the mirror. Her slippery eyes were glued to this light green cheongsam, from top to bottom, and then from bottom to top. She looked left and right, feeling that the pattern of this cheongsam was novel, the color was bright, the style was new, and it made her delicate waist even more graceful, shining on her apple-colored face especially white and delicate. In her self-satisfied mirror, she felt like a fairy in the sky, an angel in the world.

She seemed to want to show off her beauty and expect others' praise, uncontrollably leaping from the bedroom to the outside as if stepping on a Charleston dance, humming a lullaby on her lips. When she walked into the living room, she caught a glimpse of her cousin Ming chatting with her mother, which made her even more excited because she could show off the beauty of her new dress.

"Oh, Brother Ming, when did you come?" she asked him like this, while paying attention to how he would exclaim at the sight of her new dress.

"Oh, Ying, not long…" He turned around and his eyes met Ying's brand-new cheongsam, and his words suddenly stopped.

This was an unexpected disappointment to her. Not only did he not praise her, but there was clearly some anger on his face. At this time, all the hopes in her heart disappeared. She felt his strangeness and was unprovokedly despised and ridiculed by him. She felt as if she had suffered a great humiliation, and all her happiness turned into a belly full of boredom. She turned around and ran back to her bedroom in one breath, and annoyance and resentment pierced her fragile heart.

XXX XXX XXX XXX XXX XXX

Ying now understood her mistake, she woke up and regretted her recklessness. Experience told her that she must carefully consider the source of the clothing materials when buying them. Now she knew that she had been deceived by unscrupulous merchants and had become a cold-blooded animal that people condemned. She now not only did not hate him but was grateful to him, because he pointed out her mistake. She solemnly held his letter in detail and repeatedly read it, especially this paragraph in his letter:

…Even if you hate me very much, I will try my best to advise you, this is what my conscience urges me to do!

I never thought you would become so numb, decadent, and heading towards that land of no return, fighting against your own conscience and wearing enemy goods without shame! Have you forgotten the suffering you suffered in the past?

At the time of the Songhu Battle, you fled from your broken home to Shanghai in a panic. At that time, how indignant you were at the enemy's ferocity, how you beat your chest and stamped your feet, scolding the enemy's cruelty, clenching your fists and vowing to break off all relations with the enemy forever and never use enemy goods. Have you really forgotten these things?

Although the war has stopped, the enemy's ambitions are still high, you should know this, right?

In this period when the voice of promoting domestic goods is as high as the clouds, can we still not use domestic goods as much as possible?…

Free Talk

Not About Age 261

— Zhong Fang

After reading Mr. Tang Tao's "What Youth Needs," I was deeply moved and wanted to say a few words as well.

In the past, during the "May Fourth" era, those who "criticized" young people for needing "more and newer styles, powerful stimulation" seemed to be only the older generation. However, even the old-fashioned elderly at that time did not say that young people "needed to lie." But now, the young Mr. Kang Sihua is also "criticizing" young people. Furthermore, he believes that young people need to "lie." For this statement to come from within the youth themselves naturally carries even more "weight"! And there must be more than just one young Mr. Kang who holds this view.

This is one point where "now" differs from the "May Fourth" era. Back then, the phrase "conflict between father and son" was sufficient. In "now," the reasons for conflict cannot be rigidly sought based on age. Aren't there some young people today who are quite "mature and prudent," while some who are past their youth are very fiery?

The problem lies in what Mr. Kang calls "the need to lie."

Mr. Kang seems to think that he doesn't need to lie, nor does he need more new styles. But when we open our eyes and look, aren't new styles emerging endlessly? And aren't the methods of lying becoming more sophisticated day by day? In this atmosphere, is it that only those who turn a deaf ear and a blind eye, like Mr. Kang, can be said not to need to lie? Naturally, what Mr. Kang criticizes is not the "more new styles" I am talking about here, but precisely because he is like this, he has become someone who truly needs to lie. And what Mr. Kang criticizes as "more new styles" is exactly the "lying" he is criticizing.

In "now," those who do not need to lie inevitably have some "fire," even if they have not "criticized" "calm, profound, erudite speech and attitudes." It's indeed true that they don't love to read much. This is actually not about the "youth" or "old age" based on age. Just look at how the young Mr. Kang has already "testified by example"!

Pu Nuo A and the Nobel Prize 262

— Mu Mutian

The other day, I heard that this year's Nobel Prize was awarded to the author of "The Gentleman from San Francisco," Pu Ning. Yesterday, I watched the film "The Siren of the Atlantide," based on the novel by French Academy member Pu Nuo A (Pierre Benoit). These two events inadvertently connected in my mind.

I wanted to read "The Siren of the Atlantide" when I was a student, but I never managed to. Academician Pu Nuo A had traveled to the Orient and even lectured at the Hochi Shimbun's auditorium, it seems. But I never had the chance to admire his academician's brilliance. Teacher Enberkerlot was a French Catholic monk, and he highly praised this academician, calling him the modern Alexandre Dumas. I don't like Alexandre Dumas, not because he was the mixed-race child of a French man and a black woman. I really didn't enjoy reading his swashbuckling novels. It's because they weren't artistic enough. Looking back now, I'm afraid it's because he lacked progressiveness. Because I didn't like Alexandre Dumas, I also disliked Academician Pu Nuo A. Even so, I still wanted to catch a glimpse of him from time to time.

This time, Pu Nuo A's great work "The Siren of the Atlantide" actually made it to the silver screen. And the people of this semi-colonial land also had the good fortune to behold it. Moreover, the author Pu Nuo A was elected as an academician of the French Academy three years ago. When a person becomes important, their writing is always worth money. So, I had to take another look at him. And recently, someone introduced him by saying that "The Siren of the Atlantide" is full of "poetry." "Seeing is believing." So, yesterday, I went to see it.

The desert scenery is indeed captivating. Beautiful as it is, behind that beauty, it feels like there's a sharp blade stabbing my heart. This current "Alexandre Dumas," in "The Siren of the Atlantide," clearly reveals himself as a lackey of imperialism. He is like Psichari and Louis Bertrand. In his novel "The Siren of the Atlantide," isn't Pu Nuo A loudly praising France's aggression towards its African colonies? This may be the main reason why he was elected as an academician. His fantasy created that "Siren of the Atlantide," but in the end, he revealed his fox tail. What he makes us feel is only sharp blades.

It is said that in the French Academy, only the old man Anatole France was someone. To use the words of our "country bumpkins," only he "was worth his salt." This was a long, long time ago. It is said that Anatole France only visited the Academy once, during his inauguration, and never stepped foot in that "Hall of Refinement" again. After Anatole France's death, the French Academy naturally became homogeneous. It is inevitable that people like Pu Nuo A would be elected as academicians.

However, no matter what, Pu Nuo A "maintains the old style." He is the current Alexandre Dumas.

Today (Monday, the 13th), Mr. Zhili wrote the following passage in "Free Talk":

"This year's Nobel Prize, it is said, went to the Russian writer Pu Ning. And it is said: 'Born in 1870, he is a recent Russian novelist, skilled in short stories. He does not adopt the new trends of Russian literature and maintains the old style.'"

Based on the above passage, it can be inferred that next year's Nobel Prize should be awarded to the author of "The Siren of the Atlantide." Because Pu Nuo A maintains the style of Alexandre Dumas.

What I am doing here is making a "prediction." At the same time, I am making a proposal to the Nobel Prize management personnel in the capacity of a "prophet." But will the words of someone from a semi-colonial land count? Probably, people from semi-colonial lands have neither the qualification to propose nor to receive the award. Don't we also have "Burning of the Red Lotus Temple"?

Scenery of the Big Courtyard 263

— Qing Nong

From the window of my residence, I look down on a big courtyard. The southwest sides are the back walls of other alleys, and the east side is right under the window of my residence. A row of single-story houses facing south stands there. The open space in front is only about two or three zhang square. In the center, there is also a short, non-multi-story house. This is the area of the big courtyard. That row of single-story houses is divided into three rooms, and at least six families live in each room. The short house in the center also houses at least four families. There are so few houses and so many people. It's truly a wonder they can live there.

As soon as day breaks, the jazz music of the big courtyard begins, a loud and hurried ensemble. That's the sound of washing chamber pots. With a dozen or twenty chamber pots being washed, and even clam shells placed inside, what kind of sound do you think would prevent me from "rising at dawn"?

After the "jazz music" stops, women scolding husbands, mothers hitting sons, children quarreling… the sound film begins again. Do you think I can still write articles calmly?

Unable to bear the disturbance every day, I simply stand in front of the window to appreciate this beautiful scenery.

In front of the short house, a frame is built with large bamboo poles, and small bamboo poles are hung on the frame from the corridor railing of the middle house to dry clothes. Those must be the clothes of some auntie. Squeezed not dry, water is dripping. Some sister-in-law below starts to scold. And so, the two of them, without any sense of shame, begin to curse each other loudly.

There is a well in front of the first house. A dozen or twenty families rely on this well for eating, washing vegetables, and washing clothes. Some girl, with two braids hanging down and wearing a checkered cloth cheongsam, is drawing water. Some auntie standing next to her scolds her for being so slow, making people's legs ache. The girl doesn't give in, and the two of them also start cursing each other.

Buzzing in the sky, airplanes, airplanes, everyone closes their mouths, stops working, and stretches their necks to look at the sky. A little girl of eight or nine years old is holding the neighbor auntie's baby, watching the airplanes. Without warning, she trips over a stone, and the little girl and the baby fall to the ground. The baby cries loudly, and the little girl is so scared that her face turns as white as paper. The neighbor auntie rushes over and picks up the baby, repeatedly saying, "Good baby, don't be afraid." The baby's crying stops, and the little girl, now frightened, starts to cry out loud.

Big Sister Ma, with disheveled hair, is waiting for someone at the door. A woman wearing a tattered serge cheongsam enters this big courtyard from outside, constantly looking back. She walks as if hiding military supplies on her body, her frightened expression showing on her thin face. Strange, I only see her approaching Big Sister Ma, taking out a small piece of paper from the long stockings on her legs, and stuffing it into Big Sister Ma's hand along with some copper coins. Without a word, they nod to each other and separate. Big Sister, that girl with the big eyes, is standing at the entrance as a lookout. They are doing secret work for betting on flower arrangements. Then, several men and women all make contact with Big Sister Ma in the same secretive way. The girl who has the piece of paper stating the name of the flower arrangement she is betting on takes it out from her permed hair. The secret work is done with utter magic.

The sounds of cursing, loud shouts, quarrels, and children crying never stop broadcasting for a second.

In front of the short house, an old woman and an old man with white hair put down two spinning wheels and start spinning yarn, buzzing. This is a stringed violin duet, which is more peaceful and melodious than the morning brass "jazz music."

However, the "jazz music" is my prelude to "rising at dawn," while this violin duet has become the lullaby for my entire writing time.

However, on Sundays, the "Wild Rose" of the big courtyard returns. In the "violin duet," you can hear her clear singing voice, and the big courtyard is beautified.

This "Wild Rose" is the daughter of a family living in the middle house, about sixteen or seventeen years old. She has a slender figure, a pretty face, likes to wear a cheongsam made of dark blue calico, has permed hair, and wears sneakers. She is a female student studying at some school. She goes home every Saturday afternoon, and on Sundays, she often sings loudly, sometimes singing popular tunes, and sometimes singing songs taught at school. Her voice is crisp and round, probably a song and dance star at the school. She sings sometimes in the upstairs room, and sometimes she runs to the well and sings while dancing.

"Wild Rose," or maybe she's called "Wild Cat," she also often quarrels with the neighbor's girls. When she quarrels, how fierce she is. Look at how her eyes are narrowed and her lips are moving non-stop. However, as soon as she ignores people's mouths, she starts singing, such a moving singing voice.

"Wild Rose's" brother works as an informant in the police station. He leaves the house every morning when the "jazz music" is playing, a big guy, with a helmet, and black cloth pants, often reminding me of the informants I have encountered before, and evoking past memories.

Children of the Street 264

— Tang Tao

In this bitter cold, in this dark night,

Child, why do you linger on the street?

The north wind blows, you sigh like a ghost,

In this bitter cold, in this dark night.

Do you not have a mother, and a father?

What has blinded their tenderness?

In this bitter cold, in this dark night,

Child, why do you linger on the street?

Two Brothers (30) 265

— Guy de Maupassant, translated by Li Weike

For a long time, he had been lamenting his poor health, feeling heavy, and often experiencing inexplicable discomfort. The doctor said again:

"Because the bullets from a pistol can pass by your side, but the wine must enter your stomach."

"So what if it enters my stomach?"

"Then it burns your stomach, disrupts your nervous system, stagnates the blood, and makes you prone to strokes. People with your constitution are all at risk of stroke."

The increasing intoxication of the retired jeweler dissipated like a wisp of smoke in the wind: he looked at his son with an uneasy and fixed gaze, wanting to know if he was joking.

But Bao Ru cried out:

"Ah! These doctors, they are always the same: telling you not to overeat, not to drink alcohol, not to fool around with women, not to dance the polka. All of this is harmful to the body. Well! I do everything, all over the world, enjoying myself as much as possible, and my body is not doing so badly..."

Bi'er replied sternly:

"First of all, you are stronger than my father; and everyone who loves to have fun says the same thing until one day... and the next day they won't come back to tell the cautious doctor: 'Doctor, what you said before was right.' When I see my father doing something that is worst and most dangerous for him, it is only natural for me to forewarn him. Otherwise, I would be a bad son."

Feeling bored, Mother Roland came out to intervene:

"Enough, Bi'er, what's wrong with you? Just this once, it won't do him any harm. Think about how happy he is today, how happy we are. You'll completely spoil his fun and make me feel uncomfortable at home. Your behavior is too much!"

He shrugged his shoulders and murmured:

"He can do whatever he wants. I've already forewarned him."

But Father Roland stopped drinking. He looked at his glass, the glass filled with luminous wine, many small bubbles rapidly and quickly rising from the bottom of the glass and disappearing on the surface, as if the soul of this intoxicating wine was flying away; like a fox discovering a dead chicken, smelling a trap, he looked at his wine glass with suspicion.

He asked hesitantly:

"Do you think this is very harmful to me?"

Bi'er felt a kind of remorse, feeling that he shouldn't have troubled others because of his own bad mood.

"It's okay, once in a while, it's nothing, you can drink, but don't drink too much, and don't make it a habit."

So Father Roland picked up the glass, but still couldn't decide to bring it to his mouth. He stared at it painfully, wanting to drink and fearing it; then he smelled it, tasted it, drank it in small sips, savoring it carefully, while his heart was filled with bitterness, cowardice, and gluttony, and when he drank the last drop, he was filled with regret.

Bi'er suddenly met Mrs. Lu's gaze; that clear gaze rested on him, appearing discerning and stern. Bi'er felt, understood, and guessed the thoughts contained in this gaze, the thoughts of this simple and honest little woman's indignation, because this gaze seemed to say: "You're jealous, you. That's shameful."

Talking Points

Talking in Circles 266

— Cun Ren

In my student days, I was frank and outspoken, often offending others. One of my teachers taught me: "With this kind of temperament, when you go out into society, you will definitely run into walls everywhere, it's extremely dangerous. Your attitude towards people should be peaceful, never boast about your strengths, and never discuss other people's shortcomings."

"Teacher, I didn't say anything bad about others."

"Speaking without considering the other person's interests, arguing without leaving them any room, this is the same as talking about their bad points, or even more so, because it makes it impossible for them to save face. Speaking in a way that makes it impossible for someone to save face, that kind of attitude is not good."

But despite receiving instruction, my personality was already formed, mountains can be moved, but personality cannot be changed. I still often had a bad attitude when talking to people. The teacher sighed and said: "This child cannot be taught!"

After leaving school and entering society, the teacher's prediction came true, and I ran into walls everywhere. The reason for running into walls was my frankness, even to the point of offending good friends.

After hitting a wall, I sought advice from a worldly elder, a fellow villager. The elder said: "Having sharp corners, being inexperienced in the world, being hot-blooded, and lacking cultivation, you will naturally gain enlightenment from these subtle things after hitting the wall a few more times."

A few more years passed, white hair had grown, my beard had lengthened, and although I had hit the wall many times, my attitude towards people was still not good. I asked the worldly elder again. The elder said: "You've hit the wall so many times, and you still haven't gained enlightenment?"

"I understand a little. At first, I can still pretend, but after talking for a long time, my attitude still turns bad."

"Being able to pretend to talk to people, this child is already teachable. Can't you keep up the pretense all the time? Just be careful and cautious, never speak wildly, and you'll be halfway there."

"However, I would like to hear your teachings."

"For example, when exchanging pleasantries with someone, you shouldn't immediately blurt out about the hot or cold weather. Just say: 'The weather today, hahaha...' If that person says, 'The weather today is really cold,' then you can say, 'Yes, it's really cold.' That way, you won't offend anyone. Maintaining this policy of talking in circles, your speech will naturally be impeccable, and no matter how long you talk to them, your attitude will never turn bad."

However, this policy of talking in circles is not for me. I simply can't force a fake smile, and I still have a bad attitude towards people everywhere, and I still hit the wall.

Alas, how difficult, this policy of talking in circles. This life is over, but I hope that when I am reborn as a son in the next life, I will know how to talk in circles.

Remembering the Past 267

— Bing

It was two years ago.

At school, I was such a fool, disliking socializing, and even not really wanting to talk to people much. But I was often wrongly dragged into student council-like organizations to play a supporting role. In this kind of situation, the usual students are most uninhibited. They can brazenly run to the Western Palace and Eastern Palace to flirt and show off, or at least act as a tourist in the corridors there, circling around for no reason. If it attracts rumors of flirting, there's plenty of room for explanation. You're not going to collect student council dues, but you can say you're urging the school beauty to perform at the talent show, or you can say you're fundraising for "anti-Japanese" or "disaster relief." If so, let the rumors fly, and let your "cha-cha-cha" leather shoe sound (patent leather shoes may be even more fashionable) progress your mission under the oiled hair and chest-out primping.

I was really too foolish, as if poisoned by the idea that "women are trouble," and even though I sometimes had strange thoughts, I always looked down on female classmates. This may be because of my own many flaws, always wearing the same set of tattered long gowns from start to end of the year, and having a yellow-black complexion. I often felt that people like me were bound to be ridiculed by them, and it seemed to be true. Whenever I ran into them, I always felt that they were laughing at me.

It could be said that the clerk in the teaching affairs office was deliberately teasing me. This semester, he put me at the same table with a female classmate named ×. At first, I was a little angry, but I could only swallow it privately, and then I sat down at the same table with her calmly.

Although she wasn't the school beauty or princess, she had an equal reputation. A pair of sharp eyes, a torrential-sounding cherry mouth, and an easygoing attitude were some of her fundamental beauties, and the pure wine that fascinated quite a few students.

Since we sat at the same table, in order to avoid being entangled, I always arrived five minutes late, secretly dodging the teacher's gaze and slipping into the classroom. After class, my feet would rush out of the classroom as soon as the bell rang.

That way, we were at peace, and the classmates couldn't find any reason to spread rumors about me, but instead, they laughed at me as the king of fools, because quite a few students were suffering from not having the opportunity to get close to her.

Not long after, I discovered a secret about her, which was that every time I went to class, I always saw her tearing up her own notepad to wipe the dust off my desk. I thought in surprise: "Ah, women, this may be a characteristic of women!"

After that, it was every time I took the dirty things back, and even praised them a few times without reason. Knowing that she would not look at these useless things, if I didn't bring them back and asked her for them, she would always say to bring them next lesson. When I couldn't wait any longer, I had to say a thirteen-point reliable sentence: "Miss ×, please bring them back next lesson no matter what!" She didn't bring them back next lesson, so I asked her again, and she said: "Why don't you come with me to get them later!" So I strolled into their boudoir, she was so polite and dragged out many sweets. In that situation, I seemed to feel that the house was spinning, and all I could see was the swaying of the flower circles.

The term exam was approaching, and she said vaguely that she had no confidence, meaning that she wanted me to give her a hand. The term exam was approaching, and I happened to be suffering from a severe cold with a cough. When she found out, she immediately bought me a bottle of "Almond Dew" to cure it, and at the same time, under her "charming smile," she stuffed some of her essay topics and papers under my pillow. (The End)

Investigation 268

— Ping

After being sick for three days, a urgent letter from my hometown compelled me to get out of bed. Looking in the mirror while combing my hair, I couldn't believe that only three days of illness could make me look like I had been sick for three months. My chin formed an almost equilateral angle, showing that the illness had eroded the flesh of my cheeks. My nearsighted eyes seemed to sink deeper into their sockets, and my complexion was as pale as a green vegetable. However, an important matter from my hometown awaited my completion within two days.

Although it was between autumn and winter, today seemed particularly warm. Wei wore a lined cheongsam, but after climbing the stairs several times, she had already changed into a single layer shirt. I knew that the climate in the countryside was colder than in Shanghai, and I might have to stay there for a few days. Three days of illness had already brought significant changes. To protect my fragile health, I wasn't afraid of Wei laughing at me, so I put on a thick camel hair robe and also brought an overcoat. Looking at myself in the mirror, I looked too much like a opium-smoking consumptive ghost.

As the rickshaw pulled up to the train station, I saw on the clock tower that there were only five minutes left before departure. I hurriedly paid the fare, buried my head deep in the collar of my overcoat, and quickened my pace to climb the stone steps. I didn't notice a large man blocking my way. He was an investigator, naturally with a policeman behind him with a gun hanging from his waist. I immediately stopped, held out my hands, and let him pat me up and down, left and right.

Page 23

Perhaps it was because I was wearing so many clothes that his fingertips weren't sensitive enough to detect some small objects, so he couldn't find what he was looking for. Or perhaps there was some professional reason that he ordered me to open my coat? This was certainly within his official rights. If you wanted to board the train, you couldn't resist. Moreover, in Shanghai, even if you were sitting safely at home, you might encounter this kind of sudden surprise. However, I knew that I was completely innocent, and the train was about to leave in five minutes. The next passenger train would be in the afternoon, which would affect my important business in the countryside. I couldn't help but feign ignorance out of anger and asked, "Investigate what?"

"Suspicious items!" If I were to use an inappropriate analogy to describe this response, it would be as frightening as a bullet flying in from outside the window during the Shanghai battle.

Forgive me for not knowing if wearing a camel hair robe on a sunny autumn day was against the law? He searched every pocket, a wallet, a paper package, and he examined them as solemnly as if he was inspecting military maps. Finally, my socks and the inner layers of my garters were exposed in full view of everyone (I couldn't blame the surrounding crowd, because it seemed like a very worthwhile spectacle to watch). Luckily, I had gotten out of bed this morning, and my old, worn socks had already been given to the maid. Despite this solemn inspection, the train driver didn't know that such a thing had happened outside the station, and the train slowly started to move.

In the end, he didn't check the inner layer of my pants or the big red birthmark on my back. I'm sure he didn't see it, otherwise he would have screamed loudly, because my grandmother said that when I was born with the red birthmark on my back, the midwife was also shocked, which shows how startling this red birthmark is. Although he had the skills of an investigator, he certainly didn't have the midwife's experience in recognizing red birthmarks. I didn't hear him scream or see him jump, which proved that he didn't discover my red birthmark.

The train had already left. I put on my clothes and could only call the rickshaw back. He didn't seem satisfied yet and remembered my hat. Unexpectedly, he found my old office's name card inside the brim. He glanced at me and said in a voice ten million times softer than a bullet, "Sorry!"

Not to mention the friends who came to watch the show were dumbfounded, even I, the person playing the role, was somewhat stunned. Did a name card from such a small organization have such an amazing effect?

"If I had known, I would have put the box of name cards in a brocade box and kept it with me every day." Sitting in the rickshaw, I couldn't help but laugh.

When I got home, I told Wei about the inspection. I asked her where I showed obvious clues of suspicious items.

"Maybe it's because you've been sick for three days?" my wife said humorously.

I smiled and looked in the mirror at my reflection that looked like I had been sick for three months.

Returning After Chrysanthemum Viewing 269

— Qian Xu

Recently, the Shanghai Fourth Chrysanthemum Exhibition was held at the Continental Emporium on Nanjing Road. After taking the time to appreciate it once, I couldn't help but have some thoughts:

Chrysanthemums have always been praised for "grasping fragrance in their later years." Since Mr. Tao Yuanming retired to the forest because he was "out of step with the times," and enjoyed himself with chrysanthemums, comparing chrysanthemums to gentlemen, after such vigorous "promotion," the value of chrysanthemums became extraordinarily high. Therefore, regardless of elegance or vulgarity, people would always find a few pots of chrysanthemums to play with in the autumn.

The art of chrysanthemum cultivation has been improving day by day. Things that people couldn't have dreamed of in the past, such as a single chrysanthemum plant being able to bloom in two or several colors and shapes, and the flowers in a pot of chrysanthemums being able to bloom in the same size and height, can now be cultivated artificially using scientific methods, which is not surprising at all.

Judging the names of chrysanthemums based on their shape, such as: goose yellow, crab claw, etc., now seems extremely unsophisticated. It is necessary to give them very elegant names to appear different and surpass all other flowers, for example: red and white interspersed are called "Evenly Dividing Autumn Colors," and many small ones surrounding a large one are called "Stars Surrounding the Moon," and so on.

The chrysanthemums I saw this time were indeed not bad, especially the products of Jinan University and Xiaoguan Garden were particularly beautiful. Originally, this "Chrysanthemum Exhibition" was a collection of the crystallization of many people's hard work, so it was certainly not an easy task. However, after reading, admiring, and viewing it, I felt that the artificial carving was too severe, completely losing the natural and simple spirit, and only being demonically beautiful. If we were to compare it to women, then these are all young women who are about to lose their youth, and are all flamboyant beauties who have experienced the vicissitudes of life; beauty is certainly extremely beautiful, but she has already lost her innocence and her purity.

Perhaps my view is a bit too extreme, but I have another idea:

Aren't the several pots of "Juan Ying" and "Jin Mao" in Xiaoguan Garden raised on high-legged mahogany shelves? Anyone who has seen them should have a deep impression. The trunks are short, but they hang down from above, halfway down the flower stand, covered with small flowers, yellow like golden stars, white like silver light. In the chrysanthemum array, they are like cranes among chickens, with a great momentum to look down on others. However, in the countryside, by the bamboo fence, by the river bank, they also grow in the soil, but they don't have exquisite flower pots, beautiful mahogany flower stands, and no one pays attention to them: they just let the dirt stain their faces, and let cattle and sheep trample on their bodies. Even if someone appreciates them, it is just the little girls in the village who pick them and put them in their hair, but they are discarded by the roadside in less than a day. In this situation, those who are fortunate are certainly fortunate, and can jump onto the mahogany shelf and look down on their peers: but how many are destined to be buried in the grass for life!

The "Chrysanthemum Exhibition" is on the third floor of the Continental Emporium, and the "Chrysanthemum Market" is on the fourth floor. The "Chrysanthemum Market" has been open for many days, and many of the chrysanthemums are certainly not as good as the products of the "Chrysanthemum Exhibition," which are the crystallization of many people's hard work. In particular, placing these beautiful flowers under the dry, three-dimensional building makes them appear even more vulgar. Even the "Chrysanthemum Exhibition" still couldn't avoid this "problem," although the walls were hung with calligraphy and paintings by famous artists, which everyone regarded as the height of elegance.

Originally, "no matter how good the peony is, it all depends on the support of the green leaves." A luminous pearl will lose its luster when thrown on a pile of cow dung. How can things in the world be different? I remember seeing the Chrysanthemum Exhibition at Xuanwu Lake in Nanjing at this time last year. In the lake and mountains, there were red flowers and white flowers, and most of the chrysanthemums were planted in the soil. The natural atmosphere was thriving, which was much more interesting.

On the Playground 270

— Xin

丨Don't Rob Your Own People!丨

The basketball hoop was broken and couldn't be played with, so we temporarily changed our strategy and played "Captain Ball." Captain Ball is played like this: divide the whole team into two groups, A and B, and draw a line in the middle of the field. On both sides of the middle line, draw three circles of equal size, and place one person inside and outside each circle, so a total of twelve people are needed. In the field, there are Centers who can freely run and throw the ball, two each for groups A and B, for a total of four people, so a total of sixteen people are needed to play this game. I was elected as the referee. Before we started playing, I mobilized everyone like this: "Although we are on the playground, everything must still be done with discipline; those who injure someone intentionally or unintentionally should know that this is a friendly match! What we must remember is that we must not rob our own people."

So, the waves of struggle were easily stirred up; then, the two sides competed fiercely. At this time, in addition to the sound of the ball hitting, all that could be heard on the playground was a chorus of "Don't rob your own people!" "Don't rob your own people!" Ah! When I heard this sound, I felt a great surge of emotion in my heart! This faint sound of "Don't rob your own people" is a pity to only be heard on the playground. If it could be broadcast to those bastards who specialize in "robbing their own people," they would be ashamed to death!………

Fiction

Fragments of Childhood Memories (6) 273

— Lie Huo

The sun at the end of September was still terribly hot. After being exposed to it for a long time, my skin felt itchy, as if caterpillars or mosquitoes were biting me. Fortunately, the leaves had not yet fallen completely, shielding a lot of the sunlight, and the gentle autumn breeze brought a chill to soothe it, so we didn't feel too hot. Instead, we felt warm all over, which was quite pleasant.

"Fifth Sister, why do women have to sleep with men to have children? I still don't quite understand, can you explain it again!" I repeated the central question between us.

"Don't pretend to be stupid on purpose, don't you understand? I don't believe it!" What followed was a coquettish smile.

"Really, otherwise why would I ask you!" I said it myself, but I didn't believe there was any truth in my words, so my cheeks immediately turned red.

Fifth Sister brushed her thumb across my cheek and said, "How shy!" I felt even more uneasy; however, I was secretly excited, which was a natural physiological phenomenon. Then Fifth Sister embraced me in her arms, so we leaned against each other face to face, our bodies pressed very close. I felt as if I was drunk, feeling an unprecedented sense of elation.

Suddenly, the sky darkened, and the autumn thunder sounded gloomy, like beating a cowhide drum. The bushes behind the big maple tree rustled loudly. We were startled and hurried home. Mother was already puzzled that the basket was empty; and when she saw that my lips had turned blue, my cheeks were clearly different, and I was trembling all over, she knew that I was frightened, and quickly made three passes over my forehead with Yang fire, while questioning, "What happened? You're so scared. It doesn't matter that you didn't collect pine needles, tell me quickly!" I didn't answer, but just forcefully burrowed into Mother's arms, and a question arose in my mind: "Mom said that if you do something bad that can't be told, the thunder god will strike you. Is it true?" But I didn't dare to ask Mother.

(3)

That was because Mr. Du's usual flattery skills were superb. The newly arrived county magistrate was actually an old acquaintance of Mr. Du, so Mr. Du took advantage of the rice-cutting holiday in June to hurry to the county seat. It was said that before he set off, in order to buy some more fashionable clothes, he had no money, so he sacrificed his life to sell the green seedlings of thirteen mu of grain to Master Li, exchanging them for twenty silver dollars. Then he used the money to make clothes worth twelve yuan, two sets of fashionable white bamboo cloth undershirt and pants, and a piece of homemade summer cloth long gown. Naturally, it wasn't the famous Liuyang summer cloth. It took Mrs. Du a lot of time to bleach it to make it relatively white; but it still couldn't get rid of its earthy smell and muddy taste.

Mrs. Du was somewhat dissatisfied with Mr. Du's grand gesture: "Selling the green seedlings to find a job, what if you find one? If you don't, then we'll be starving in the second half of the year, it's a disaster!" "This can be considered taking a great risk in the world!" Mrs. Du is, after all, Mrs. Du, influenced by Teacher Du, and her words are more sophisticated than those of ordinary village women, very concise: and naturally somewhat in line with modern logic.
